when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的事情是 , 說未來將會遠遠遠超過這一點 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個人來了 , 艾倫•圖靈在1936年發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然babbage的機器完全是機械性的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都來自數學的觀點 , 但 , 圖靈告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 並說: 「 不論你如何製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你電腦的機械機制 , 像是babbage的電力 , 或像現今的電腦 , 或未來的細胞 , 或者 , 又或者 , 再一次的 , 一旦我們進入奈米技術 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 。 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 電腦的本質是如此 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說這東西babbage是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到今天我們用電腦做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道它有多慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用的是打卡片 , 被放進去 , 它的第一個zx81 , 000倍慢了一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它確實有鐵包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以再加上很多記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天能帶給我們什麼樣的 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞士 , 科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯巴貝奇所寫 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組計劃我們稱之為計劃28 , 這也是我和doronswaade開啟的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的計算機策劃者 , 也是驅動這個計劃建造不同的引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓這裡 , 我們將建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有好幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一是babbage的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是一台電腦模擬這台機器的模擬 , 最後一部分是實體在在科學博物館裡製造 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它建成時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為不是在你面前有一小片晶片 , 你得要看著這個幽默的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作的聲音 。 我可能聞到它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這兩者之間我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫下 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎出現 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學軌道 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有蓋過它 , 因為他總是在小心設計新計畫 , 但當它實現時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給你們一些味覺 , 看看它在動作的樣子 , 它只顯示了cpu運作的其中一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加上 。 這是在行動中加入的機制 , 所以你會想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們就有了 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這張圖片中 , 雅恩•藝術人先生展示了他的三項近期人性 , 以及我們的棲息地 , 令人震驚的空拍攝 , 來自世界各地的個人訪問 , 他的網路專案 「 六十億人 」 , 他很快就被拍攝到的電影 , 他的家園 , 透過呼吸影片記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影、攝影照片 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅恩•亞瑟伯特在廣闊的地球上捕捉到脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡是要談生態學 , 一年內就釋放出二氧化碳 ,
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式做碳排放 , 就像我每次都做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年所拍攝的照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達•沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達人工作了24小時 , 每七個小時 , 提煉出更多的油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的盡頭 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是一個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油多出三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	珊瑚礁位於紐卡里亞 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能因為全球暖化而被消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 去年夏天我拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	大西洋和太平洋之間有個新方法 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年就降低了40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰 , 吉里曼jaro就有了新的面貌 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家100年來 , 所有山冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命很重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	如同高爾所說 , 有二十億人住在喜馬拉雅的冰河上 。
return of fish men .	回來的魚類男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	人類的五分之一取決於魚類生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 有70%的魚類被過度使用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao , 如果我們不改變我們在2050年捕撈主要海資源的系統 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	美麗的照片是在非洲的 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	六個人中有六個人沒有足夠的食物 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 百分之九十的玉米培育被用來餵養動物或石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅的棕櫚樹種植 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每年 , 我們在森林砍伐中損失了五萬平方英里 。
refugee camp in darfur .	丹佛的難民營 。
today we have 20 million refugees in the world .	現今世界上有兩千萬難民 。
according to the u . n . , we speak about 250 million refugees in 2050 .	根據聯合國的說法 , 我們在2050年說了兩億五千萬難民 。
i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。
we have done already 100 exhibitions in the cities .	我們已經在城市裡完成了100次展覽 。
but how to understand the world without the voice of people ?	但要怎麼去了解這個世界 , 卻沒有人的聲音 ?
landscape was not enough .	地景不夠 。

seventh man: we invented stories , we flew around the world , while remaining in our attic .	第七個男人:我們發明了故事 , 我們飛遍世界 , 還留在我們的閣樓裡 。

12th man: if i was to go back to iraq and speak to the people , i'd have to bow down and kiss their feet .	第十二個男人:如果我回到伊拉克 , 和人民說話 , 我就得要向下弓 , 親吻他們的腳 。
just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	就如同那位女士在親吻我的腳的時候 , 我們帶著她的兒子 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	他們的力量讓我感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠會覺得伊拉克有必要做回應 。
second woman: dad , mom , i grew up .	第二個女人:爸爸 , 媽媽 , 我長大了 。
you shouldn't worry about me . dad doesn't need to go to work .	你不該擔心我 , 爸爸不用去工作 。
my family . . . what can i say ?	我的家人......我能說些什麼 ?
at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	此刻 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 我在深圳的這一生 , 只是為了讓我的父母能賺得更多 , 讓我的父母能留下來 , 有些可以活下去 。

after many people said i couldn't do that .	許多人說我做不到 。

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟你們談我的電影 。
for the last three years , i was shooting the earth for the movie .	過去三年 , 我拍攝了電影 。
the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	這部電影的名字是 「 家 」 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球有四十五億年的歷史 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 數億年 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經直立行走了2萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經適應了 , 並且征服了整個星球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬種居住在我們旁邊的物種 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去三十年來 , 我幾乎看過地球和它的dweller從天上升起 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活和地球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們仰賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚 , 繁殖 , 農業仍然是世界上人類主要的職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起的 , 遠比我們分裂的更大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都一樣 , 對於地球的禮物 , 同樣的需求 , 希望能升高自己 , 並變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而我們卻繼續靠牆壁來阻擋我們 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到50年 , 我們已經徹底改變了它 , 比人類的整個歷史更加徹底 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的資源很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源無法永續發展 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們自己瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒了解到 , 我們的速度比地球還快很多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可用的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們還在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的這場演講中 , 理查•雷斯尼克展示了如何便宜且快速的基因定序 , 即將把健康照護轉換為上下 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、科技、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上方 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角的是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大型x染色體 ; 男人有x , 當然 , 那個小型的y 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起的男孩們 , 但這只是一個小東西 , 讓你改變了 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 你當然會看到這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼 , 將這四個生物化學字母拼出來 , 或者我們稱之為基礎:a、c、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以投入大量的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280像素的每一個像素放到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3 , 000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順便說一下 , 有一群人 , 有y染色體決定要定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序 , 出版了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後的版本被發表 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是用像這樣的機器完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一鹼基都要花一塊美金 , 非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道這件事 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	我們現在做的是把基因組做50張複製品 , 把這些複製品切成五十頁 , 然後我們定序它們 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把它帶到軟體裡 , 把它重新組合 , 告訴你故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給你一張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gabes , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器 , 一週內有200gb 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將有200人改變600人的速度沒有減速的跡象
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基地的價格 , 排序一個基地 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年裝滿氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星和背部兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、古老的排序方式 , 還有所有新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是一個流行規模 , 通常你不會看到像這樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界對於人類基因組序列的能力大約是今年約五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被安置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期這會增加兩倍 , 三倍或四倍 , 可能是可預見的未來一年 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別是有一個實驗室 , 佔了百分之二十的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對贏得了新月球的比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學來說是什麼意思 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	女性年齡是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她帶著2個雌激素受體乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和輻射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三顆卵巢癌回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 手術和化療再次治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時 , 得到更多卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又帶著急性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸道失敗 , 八天後就死了 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被治療的方式 , 在短短的十年內 , 看起來會像血液流動 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	那是因為像我同事rickwilson的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 他決定去看這位婦女的後遺症 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他定序 , 吃下皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚、癌症的骨髓 , 他定序了兩種基因組 , 在幾個星期內 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩組基因組和軟體比較 , 他發現 , 在其它的東西當中 , 是一個刪除 , 在三十億個鹼基中 , 有兩千多個鹼基 , 一種特殊基因 , 叫做tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果基因中有這種致命的突變 , 你就有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒有幫助 , 但如果你願意的話 , 這對她的家庭有很大的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測試 , 然後他們明白了 , 這樣他們就可以定期檢測出癌症 , 可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我介紹一下啤酒雙胞胎 , 在二歲的時候被診斷出腦性麻痺症 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位很勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不符合 , 透過一些英雄式的努力和網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是帕斯頓尼亞 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了 「 烏托邦 」 , 他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但他們並沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片中的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙他很幸運成為一家叫做生命科技的公司
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是製造這些大量基因定序工具的兩家公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是讓他的孩子排序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一系列的突變 , 在一個叫做 「 春天 」 的基因中 , 它負責產生血清素 , 其它東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在dopa之上 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素前期藥物 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有完整的基因定序 , 這絕對不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	當時是幾年前 , 花費10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	現在是一萬美金 , 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	百元後的那一年 , 給予或一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有一些小小的nick喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 腹部像個飢荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	牠不是在吃 , 而是當牠吃的時候 , 牠的腸道基本上會打開 , 糞便會流出牠的腸道 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	幾百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我祈禱 , 我非常痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生恰好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但是他說: 「 我們拿到這個孩子的基因序列 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現一個單點突變 , 在控制細胞死亡的基因中 , 一個單點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對食物的反應有一些免疫反應 , 基本上就是 , 這種反應會導致一些編寫的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管制下的基因被破壞了 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫展示他的骨髓礦工一個新的裝置 , 能快速收集生命的骨髓 , 和捐贈者的最小痛苦 。 他強調的是 , 骨髓的成人幹細胞可以被用來治療許多終止的條件 , 從帕金森森氏症到心臟病 。

we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 以拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收割這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個or.團隊 , 一般麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生 , 來自我 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌上 , 我們用這種小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們做這件事的方式基本上就是把這個裝置放在軟組織裡 , 把它打到硬骨頭裡 , 到塔丘上 , 每次有十個骨髓 , 每次用針筒打出十個骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 , 她把它送到一個小東西裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們一而再再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是200次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我手臂的尾聲是如此 , 我手上有aus , 更不用說鮑伯 , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個手術在40年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能還有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個最小侵入性的方法 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式就是這裡的 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準種子病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不再進入骨骼的十幾次 , 而是進入髖骨的前面或髖骨的後方 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性的導體 , 有特殊的電線路口 , 留在馬路的殘酷部分 , 跟著臀部的交通工具 , 隨之而來 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	它能讓你快速地吸入骨髓 , 或是吸出一個洞 , 非常快速地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過相同的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能收到一口口口 , 當地麻醉劑 , 把這個收穫當作是門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛拿到一小塊錢 。
and played around with this a little bit .	玩了一點點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終 , 我們有兩個大型動物 , 還有豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 驚訝的是 , 我們不只得到骨髓 , 我們還得到了十倍的幹細胞活動 , 從骨髓的骨髓 , 和一般的裝置做比較 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年就被核准了 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活體病患 。 你可以看到它在附近的彈性曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	同一個病人 , 在同一個洞裡 , 就會有兩個通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉劑 , 做為治療 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞數量是同一個病人的標準方法的三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是個非常豐富的成人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞在我們身體的整個過程中 , 包括我們骨髓的血液幹細胞 , 我們用這種幹細胞治療已經超過40年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年間 , 使用骨髓幹細胞的爆發 , 來治療病人其他疾病 , 像是心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛推出 , 我們正在商業化 , 今年 , 第二代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能讓更多幹細胞被翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人參與成為可能救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你可以銀行你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年輕、健康的時候 , 讓你可以在未來使用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植倖存者 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家garretgarretgarretlisi在宇宙中有爭議性的新模型 , 可能只能回答所有的大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是你見過最美麗的8維元元素模型 , 強迫你見過 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi理論上所有東西的理論都是garretlisi
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 , 看看那些殺手方程式 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能地描述無方程式的粒子物理的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭包含數千隻珊瑚蟲 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚蟲不斷地生長 , 分枝在基因上相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以單獨找出一個人 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點與他的鄰居相比 , 如果只是偶然 , 或命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	把溫度轉得太高之後 , 他會告訴我們這個問題完全愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚很有意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤痕來證明它 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這隻珊瑚蟲會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居非常明顯地是同類的 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其它地方 , 但經歷了它們和獨立個體一樣 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分枝不同的珊瑚蟲是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級聰明的珊瑚會特別準備好了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷分開成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪的現象最早被erwinschrdinger和他的貓所描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個組合中 , 薛丁格和放射性樣本放入一個盒子裡 , 通過量子力學的定律 , 分枝進入一個狀態 , 而不是放射和一個狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在採集樣本的分支中 , 它啟動了釋放毒素和薛丁格的觸發器已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一種層面 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些實相被分開了 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	到目前為止 , 另一種並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人只經歷一個人的存在 , 而我們不會看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格一樣 , 是一種珊瑚的分支 , 一種不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 世界是如此運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	剩下的物理則是描述可能發生什麼事 , 什麼都不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 所有東西都歸功於幾何 , 以及基本粒子的互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼 , 以及平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子會加速接近光速 , 以碰撞產生出純能量的爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這股能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里的周圍 , 當它在運作時 , 比蒙特雷市的電力還要多出5倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法特定地預測出哪些粒子會在任何個體碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須的質量和能量就跟質子和反質子一樣 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這能源限制更大的粒子 , 都不會產生出來 , 對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新的粒子加速器非常令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會推動這個能量極限 , 超越以前所做過的事 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我來描述我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一大堆亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部份人熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	這裡的許多人 , 讓很多人活得很好 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中性伴侶 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上夸克的質量非常大 , 三分之一的結合 , 使質子和中子在原子裡 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都在左邊 , 右邊的多樣性 , 有相反載荷的抗粒子伴侶 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉第二代和第三代 , 和第一代相同的載荷相同 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都和各種力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過稱為光子的粒子相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種很弱的力量 , 很不想像力 , 只和左撇子物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克的強力作用是帶有一種不同的載荷 , 叫做色荷 , 三種不同的物質:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以責怪murraygellmann , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的力量 , 會透過質量和旋轉來互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一種力量有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量相互作用 , 根據每個粒子有的相對應的載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個尚未被發現的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 給予質量給所有其他粒子 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的就是看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎題是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一個美麗的可能性 , 朝這次演講結束 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 就會有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子來追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然有好多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的載荷來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷就是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個夸克和下方夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它總有一電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷實際上是另外兩種電荷組合:超級充電和弱電荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超音波和弱電荷散開 , 在這二度載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會根據超連結和弱荷來互動 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 民選模式 」 , 它在1967年被組合起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊這邊的希格斯有很大的質量 , 破壞了這個發電模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力非常弱 , 讓弱粒子大到大 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯沿著水平方向 , 電磁學的光子仍然是無質的 , 與電荷的垂直方向相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力是由二度空間中的粒子載荷所描述的 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力推廣它的兩個載荷方向 , 並在這些方向上畫出夸克力粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知的粒子的載荷可以在四度的載荷空間中畫出來 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 大自然就會保持完美的平衡 , 同時也是這四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它就會產生一股能量 , 且在四個載荷方向的總載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西只要它有相同的能量 , 就能保持零的總載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	舉例來說 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 指控總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐化成電子 , 一顆中子 , 這三顆仍然會增加到零總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不只漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 哪些互動被允許發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四維空間旋轉這個載荷空間 , 更好地觀察強烈的交互作用 , 它有很好的六角形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強力粒子 , 例如這顆 , 與有色的夸克互動 , 例如這顆綠色夸克 , 給予不同顏色的夸克 , 紅色的 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每一秒就會發生數百萬次 , 以我們身體的每一個原子組合 , 將原子核黏在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還能把兩個載荷和重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把這些粒子納入 , 每個粒子都有兩種不同的旋轉 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開 , 在六度載荷空間中 , 給出一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間旋轉這個模式 , 看看它是很漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們目前所知的大自然在這些元素的微小尺度 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在實驗中非常有限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小的粒子物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要談談一些我們還不知道的新點子 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們只想用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否掌握全部的手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有的粒子和力量 , 來完成我們宇宙的圖像 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子在實驗到更高的能量時會看到的 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	粒子物理學有一個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷模式 , 不對稱的 , 可以從更完美的模式中出來 , 以至於希格斯粒子破壞了電荷模式 , 來產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引進新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子在這個方向的載荷 , 然後我們可以把它轉換成另一個方向 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六度載荷空間中建構出標準載荷的對稱性 , 以七度載荷的方式 , 來對稱這個更完美的模式 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種選擇對應到1973年由帕蒂和薩拉姆引進的大統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到一些缺口 , 粒子似乎是缺少的 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 包含了特定的圖案 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新的粒子存在 , 它應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七維空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 考慮到關於粒子的奇怪事實:第二和第三代物質在六度載荷空間中有完全一樣的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子不被六個載荷分辨出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在一個標準載荷空間上 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能分配每個粒子獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中轉動 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二和第三代相關的物質 , 由所謂的 「 審判 」 的對稱性 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度空間的載荷模式實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大例外的謊言團體e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 曲線形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這圖案中的每一個點 , 都會對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學結合 , 這個形狀的幾何圖形可以描述宇宙是如何運作的 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種八度載荷空間的形狀是非常美麗的 , 它將數千個可能的互動結合在這些元素粒子之間 , 每一個都是這個複雜的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 我們可以看到其中許多複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉 , 我們就能在八度空間中觀察這個模式 , 同時觀察到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一物 , 我們可以看到一些由這個模式所需要的新粒子 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	有20個缺口 , 新粒子應該被填滿 , 其中兩個粒子則被帕地山粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新的粒子應該是比如希格斯粒子 , 但有顏色的載荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 給我們全e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的觀點:這個偉大數學美的物體可以用最小的尺度描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	這種由數學所描述的大自然並不是全新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這篇文章: 「 大自然的偉大之書 , 不斷地對我們的目光打開 , 用數學的語言寫 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有任何一個字是人道不可能理解的 ; 沒有這些字在黑暗的迷宮中漫步的 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 描述粒子物理學的數學 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何數字 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家一起工作時 , 數學可以和黑暗的迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但要確保數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 隨著不斷成長的e8珊瑚 , 每個粒子在各種可能的地點 , 以一種美麗的模式互動 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式 , 使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們可能會看到大自然使用這個e8的圖案或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現過程是很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那就會非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論來說不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作方式是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論是長時間拍攝 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人真的很努力地知道 , 大部分這些點子可能不會成為自然的真相 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理學就是這樣:有很多的擦力 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有大量的投資 , 就很難拋棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得要去嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要維持公平和幸福的唯一方法 , 就是保持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡我所能去平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡物理、愛、衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣 , 即使我所研究的物理都沒有 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年來 , 我住在馬伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是我父母在宇宙中最偉大的謎題之一 , 讓我無法隨時地存活下來 , 卻沒有全職員工 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	接下來我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊市的家鄉辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能注意到這些美麗的觀點相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活的遊牧場有時很困難 , 但它讓我生活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我的生活中 , 我一直很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明的人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能被邀請來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概知道其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你對所有事物的理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 至少有幾個人很興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該想到宇宙 , 它的心 , 最小的東西 , 是e8物體的可能性嗎 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度下 , 是否有一個尺寸 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我給你們看的圖案 , 和我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這也是我說我們知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 它融入了e8模式 , 可能是照片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我剛剛給你們看的這些點 , 其實代表的是高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、跳舞、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論學家 , 我了解它 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該怎麼看待e8的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 它是e8形狀的一種對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會轉動 。 當它移動時 , 它會轉動的方向是我們所見到的粒子 。 克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關聯 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它是更大嗎 ? 它比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降低到最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都同時擴張和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用比喻珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	以這種方式 , e8來源的方式是每次空間時間的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀的方向會隨著曲線的表面移動而扭曲的形狀是元素本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們會以點的形式呈現 , 並以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能否更清楚一點 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這並不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它會喚起一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然想要更了解它 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	非常謝謝你來 。 這真是令人著迷 。

jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍古德能協助人類和動物在一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 喔 , 喔 , 喔 , ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ 喔 ~ 喔 ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ 喔 ~ ~ ~ ~ ~
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡前所做的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一邊 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今晚我想跟大家談談 , 昨天的zeray留下來的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇、三歲的澳大利亞孩童塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽到了人類的歷史 , 人類的家族樹 , 由dna遺傳資料來描述 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一個古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯•雷克 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時是非常不凡的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你還可以分辨出那些化石的樣子 , 從肌肉的形狀 , 從肌肉的生存方式 , 從各式各樣的工藝品中發現的樣子 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的物種、大猩猩和人類身上找到類似的行為模式 , 那麼也許這些行為出現在七百萬年前 , 人類祖先中 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們已經把這些特性從古老的過去帶給我們這些特徵 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今處理人類演化的教科書 , 通常會發現人們會推測人類早期的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何其他生物都更像我們 , 在ted會議中 , 我們已經聽說過了 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 對我來說 , 黑猩猩在某些方面是如此相似的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給他們名字 。 他們可以活到60年或更久 , 不過我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 雌螢火蟲在十一或十二歲時 , 牠的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五或六年就有一個寶寶 , 一個長期的童年依賴 , 當孩子在護理時 , 晚上和媽媽一起睡覺 , 背後還騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信長期的童年期對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就如同對我們來說 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更複雜所以我們發現學習在個人生命歷史上扮演著更重要的角色
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察他們的長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式 , 目前在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中所看到的不同的隔離行為 , 研究這些行為是如何通過一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和做法 , 來形容這些獨立的行為是原始的文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 。 我們已經談過這件事了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	它們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 許多都相似 , 甚至相同的 , 在同樣的情境下形成 , 希臘的黑猩猩擁抱著 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍手 ,
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們會游泳 , 會丟石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多關於同情心的例子 , 愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的天性有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常激烈 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比其他生物更能幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和其它動物界之間並沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 每當我們觀察到更多時 , 它就會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍然持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 活在他們複雜的社會生活 , 幫助我們了解到我們是其中的一部分 , 而不是和我們共享地球的驚人動物分開 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很可悲的發現黑猩猩 , 像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是空氣中的一張照片 , 它會讓你看到gombe的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約16年前 , 我飛越整個區域 , 發現在公園之外的這片森林 , 在1960年 , 在坦尼卡的東岸 , 幾乎沒有破碎 , 也就是在那兒的三十平方公園 , 那個問題來了我腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 ? 當這些住在國家公園的人們掙扎著生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那裏 , 比土地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民湧入緬甸的數量從剛果的湖中增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人無法從其他地方購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這就導致了我們所謂的tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的改善生活方式 , 來改善生活在公園裡的人們 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村落開始 , 現在是24個村莊 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去探討它 , 但它包括樹木護士 , 目前最適合的農業方法 , 幾乎是沙漠降落在這些山區 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、防止土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	復興過量的農田 , 讓兩年內 , 再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民取得乾淨的水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和少數女性合作 , 提供她們機會給微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們有95%的貸款回來 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	讓女性有權力 , 和教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓他們能完成中學院 , 明確地了解全世界 , 身為女性的教育 , 家庭大小降低 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 保育發生了什麼事 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育正在發生的是 , 居住在這24個村莊的農民 , 而不是把我們看成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 很多的員工都是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計程時 , 這是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 當情況開始改善時 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山頂的上層被樹木砍伐 , 所以你就有了這種可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園之外的一個面積 , 向外延伸到各個非常退化的土地 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意把10%到20%的土地放在高地邊緣 , 所以 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩會通過這些黑猩猩的走廊 , 讓牠們可以在國家公園以外的遺傳性與其它的遺傳性團體互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 塔瑞是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲其他地方複製它 , 在其他地方 , 面對極端人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題如同我們過去幾天都在討論這些ted的所有日子 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮有很多 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	而當你有大量的土地居住在不那肥沃的土地 , 尤其是當你砍樹的時候 , 土壤會對土壤開放 , 造成絕望的人口減少更多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能試著為自己和家人種植食物 , 有什麼事會發生 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	其他的問題不只在非洲 , 還在開發中國家 , 確實 , 無所不在 , 無所不在 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.wilson說 , 如果地球上的每一個人都能維持普通的歐洲人或美國人的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 , 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這個問題是 , 我們是 , 最聰明的人 , 走過地球 , 帶著非凡的大腦 , 能夠被這些ted研討會所描述的科技 , 然而我們卻毀了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決定之前 , 常常會問自己: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們七個世代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我不是特別談非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 涉及數百萬美金 , 通常都是基於 「 這會如何影響到下一個股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定影響著非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行時 , 談到黑猩猩和森林面臨的問題 , 我了解到越來越多的非洲問題 , 可能會在過去的殖民地爆發 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始到非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲聊天 , 在美國聊天 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我所說的 , 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水可能是我們本世紀面對的最關鍵問題之一 , 到處都是 , 被污染的農業、工業和家庭的化學物質污染 , 這些化學物質仍然在世界各地噴灑 , 似乎似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲益 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 , 海嘯的效應越來越糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤的侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們對化石燃料的燃燒方式和其他溫室氣體燃燒 , 稱為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人都開始相信氣候上發生了什麼事 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而那是影響更糟的窮人 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱變得更糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來臨時 , 它通常會導致洪水 , 加上痛苦 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個無法支援的地區的人數太多無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地已經被降低了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的珊瑚礁 , 令人毛骨悚然的珊瑚礁 , 最後一棵樹被砍下來 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這種非凡聰明的大腦之間有某種區別嗎 ? ted科技的爆炸 , 人類的心 ? 以非科學的角度來說 , 在愛和同情的角度 , 有沒有其他的連結 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是憂鬱或熱情、痛苦、憤怒 。 他們說的多或少是一樣的: 「 我們會覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 而我們什麼都不做 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 自從我的年紀開始 , 我就感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這也導致了我們稱之為根與芽的計畫 , 起源於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經擴散到全世界的97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 樹根是堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	槍擊看起來很小 ; 要到達太陽 , 能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆當作我們對地球、環境、社會所造成的所有問題 , 這是一種希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地有成千上萬的年輕人可以打破 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息是:每個人每天都會有所改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有選擇去做什麼樣的差異 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人沒有選擇 。 重點是我們要改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根部和槍擊團體都選擇三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	它取決於他們有多老 , 不論他們是哪個國家 , 不論是城市或鄉下 , 都要看他們是哪些計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有來自幼兒園的計畫 , 透過大學 , 越來越多的成年人開始自己的根部和槍擊團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體之間的選擇 , 三種不同的專案計畫 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 認知到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一項計畫是幫助他們自己的社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募到錢來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是幫助動物不只是野生動物 , 家畜也是 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的計畫之一就是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切中 , 包含了一種學習的訊息 , 傳達給我們自己、在我們的家庭、在我們的社區、國家、文化、宗教、和自然界之間的連結 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能在我們的速度下破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只選其中一兩項項項目 , 在非洲 , 根與芽的團體 , 只有一兩項項項目 , 在坦尚尼亞、肯亞、南非、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說的 , 它在世界上97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 用雞蛋來賣卵 , 或是用它們來餵養家人 , 感受到驕傲和賦權 , 因為他們不再有助於他人 , 依靠蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理幫助 , 給予外在士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的專案計畫 , 讓他們自己脫離 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以現在沒有更多根和芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要元素 , 年長的孩子和年輕人交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	像這樣的事 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的傾聽 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你看過黑猩猩數量減少了大約一百萬隻 , 在本世紀初 , 到目前為止已經超過十五萬隻 , 和許多其他動物都一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能參加像ted這樣的研討會 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是神奇的大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我非常激動人心 , 來談談堆肥車道 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把所有的水都沖到電梯裡 , 真的很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	談到可再生能源的重要性 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎我們的孩子的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪女 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否在乎他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做一些選擇 , 來選擇我們每天的生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其它東西 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted能幫助我們的人 , google也幫助我們 , esri幫助我們繪製戈米貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你們今年下午聽說過這件事 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 , 若要改變 , 我們就必須要去關心未來 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	而希望大自然的下一個理由是非常有恢復力的 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個絕對被摧毀的區域 , 只要時間 , 或許就能讓它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	舉個例子 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴過你 , 看似死掉的樹木木木頭 , 如果你阻止它們破解 , 你不需要因為木很多 , 那麼在五年內 , 你就可以有一棵三十英尺長的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	幾乎在滅絕的邊緣上 , 動物可以給予第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它鼓舞人心 。 它帶領我最後一類的希望 , 過去兩天 , 我們都聽說過這一點:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這個人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 這樣你認為會因為貧窮、疾病而被打擊 , 或其他的 , 可以讓他們自己脫離貧窮 , 或疾病 , 或其它 , 有時 , 有時可以幫助他們參與社會 , 並參與改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 在非洲 , 有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
