we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但很顯然 , 尼爾森•曼德拉 , 從十七年的硬體勞動 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著寬恕的能力 , 讓他能夠帶領他的國家走出種族隔離的邪惡 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的薩洛瓦 , 採用巨大的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人盡力 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人很鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 我們需要年輕的非洲人 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 今天我聽過其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會 , 能再次和ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望有些人能聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根和芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個字 , 那個正在參加這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 用她的證書 。 她是根和芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在達瑞沙拉姆的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這可以幫助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 這對我來說是非常令人興奮的 , 看看一個例子 , 說明年輕人如何賦予權力 , 因為有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 明天是我們的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家戴安娜•柯恩分享了一些關於海洋的塑膠污染、生活和想法 , 以及如何解放我們自己 , 來解放塑膠垃圾 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠等 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	戴安娜•柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是一位視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 把它們切成縫 , 再縫合成我藝術品的主要材料 , 過去二十年來我的工作 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩三度空間的碎片、雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	與塑膠合作後 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始分裂 , 分裂成小小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	它就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	自從教導我更進一步了解塑膠 , 我意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成比較小的部分 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現在海洋環境中有很多東西 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾和垃圾 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是 , 很多人的第一反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提案 , 用貨船和兩艘退化的捕魚拖車 , 一台拖車、一台拖車 , 和一台冷貨機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是去gyre , 提高對這個議題的意識 , 然後開始把塑膠晶片放進小小的碎片裡 , 把它冷藏成磚塊 , 可以被用來當作低調社區的建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些曾經去過健身房的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且在做這件事時 , 我意識到 , 清理它會是個非常小的滴 , 相對於全世界每天生產多少東西 , 我需要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們需要找到一種方法來關掉錯誤 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單一或可丟棄的塑膠 , 這些塑膠每天都在全球各地進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這一點 , 我了解到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 而是你試著想像在太平洋中間 , 我學到的 , 現在有11個健身房 , 可能是全世界五大洋的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我所關心的不只是塑膠垃圾 , 而是超市的塑膠垃圾 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是塑膠包裝 , 即使是在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱中的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和塑膠從塑膠進入我們體內的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個問題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫正在努力 , 但當中有些很基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的80%到90%到90%的海洋碎片是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書籍 , 都以回收的理念來維持和環保 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放到一邊 , 你不需要再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	到底是什麼樣的現實 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的仔細研究一下 , 尤其是當涉及到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分的瓶子都只會下降 , 或被送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它會被拆解 , 變成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶會再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次被用來當塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再次成為塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在看的東西 , 請大家思考的是 , 我們把第四個環加到 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 、 「 三個r 」 , 也就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時 , 都會拒絕單一使用和可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 而不是用它們來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易撿起一瓶無形的瓶子或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅途中旅行 , 你就忘了帶著無形的鋼瓶 , 裝滿水或過濾水 , 反而購買塑膠瓶水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想在這裡對大家說些什麼 , 我知道你們對這個議題了解很多 , 就是這在海洋中是個大問題 , 但我們作為消費者所創造的問題 , 卻能解決這個問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對這個問題和教導人們選擇選擇的意識來解決這個問題 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 每當可能 , 選擇單一使用塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹細胞帶入海洋中 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的星球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	來自麻省理工學院的pattimaes實驗室的示範 , 由pranavyy's推行的 , 是ted的pz 。 它是一台可穿戴的裝置 , 帶著投影機去與環境互動 。 想像一下 , 少數人的報告 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技、科技等 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattimaes和pranavdedemoes第六感測器 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣:我們是否可以進化或發展出第六感 , 一種可以讓我們無縫且容易取得的溝通 , 或可能存在的資訊 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 來決定我們要面對的一切 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們當中有些人可能會說 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經這樣做了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不行 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見到某人時 , 當然是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能拿出手機和谷歌嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者當你去超市 , 站在那龐大的衛生紙堆裡 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 試著判斷哪些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得這些相關的資訊 , 來協助我們做出最佳的決定 , 來決定下一步要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組已經開發了一系列的發明 , 讓我們以簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 而不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 大部分的努力都還在進行中 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在穿著這個裝置 , 我們把它和架上的零件混合在一起 , 順帶一提 , 目前只有350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜帶、電池充電的投影系統 , 一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件會在口袋裡傳達我的手機 , 用來當作溝通和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這段影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕拉•米特里 , 他是被實踐和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何表面 , 開始用他的雙手和前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四個重要的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著簡單的標記帽子 , 你可能認得出來 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更健全的版本 , 你也可以用不同的顏色來畫指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上會追蹤這四個手指 , 辨識出他正在製作的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以去看一段長灘、放大等等的地圖 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具象徵性的姿勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 姿勢 , 然後拍下你面前的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何牆上 , 投影他拍的照片 , 整理這些照片 , 然後將它們放大 , 等等 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 在座有些人可能在兩年前來到這裡 , 看過這個示範 , 有些人可能會想: 「 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也使用自然手勢 , 兩隻手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以使用 , 並與這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 可以......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是行動裝置 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異是 , 在大量生產中 , 明天這不會比現在的手機還多 , 其實不會像一個更大的包裝 , 看起來會比我穿的脖子還多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除了讓你們當中一些人覺得很酷的幻想 , 湯姆克魯斯在《少數報導》中很興奮的原因是 , 我們對這個裝置感到非常興奮的原因之一 , 是因為它真的可以扮演一種第六感的裝置 , 讓你知道你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納進入超級市場 , 他在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統就能辨識出他撿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘色燈光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特殊的選擇是特別好的選擇 , 因為他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想要有最多麻煩的衛生紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就能拿到亞馬遜評分 , 書的封面就會被投射出來 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是juan的書 , 我們先前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 在亞馬遜有很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , pranav轉換了這本書的頁面 , 再看看這本書的讀者留言 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向某個特定的頁面 , 他可能是一位朋友的專家 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何事 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你閱讀的事件的影片註解 , 你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是更具爭議性的 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某個人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個標籤的雲 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁連結在一起的字眼 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你到機場的路上 , 如果你拿起登機 , 它可以告訴你你的飛機被延遲 , 門已經改變了 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的時光就像在手臂上畫一支手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前所處的第六感給我們無縫的資訊 , 提供我們關於我們可能遇到的事物的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕拉 , 真的 , 像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實值得很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去的三個月裡睡得太多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也不太開心 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不完美 , 它在進步中非常多 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在未來的十年 , 我們將會在這裡 , 終極的第六感植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里斯和艾瑞瓦菲有種強大的友誼 , 出生於不可思議的失敗 。 羅德里格斯的兒子在2001年9月11日被殺害 ; 艾波菲的兒子祖魯斯•莫薩伊被定罪於這些攻擊中的角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩個媽媽必須明白並尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治議題、政治議題、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:找到寬恕、友情的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有許多人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現 , 我兒子在2001年9月11日早上去世貿中心 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	直到36個小時之後 , 我們才不知道他是否已經滅絕了 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治性的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們很害怕我們的國家會以我們兒子的名字來做些什麼 , 我的兒子 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	然而當我看到它時 , 令人震驚的震驚 , 以及我們人生中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有毒 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後 , zacariasmoussaoui被指控了六個圖像 , 針對恐怖主義 , 而美國政府要求他死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我的丈夫和我公開反對 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些人權團體 , 我們和幾個受害者的家人聚集在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我看到媒體上的阿西哈 , 她兒子被指控時 , 我心想: 「 什麼是勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要見到那位女士 , 我更強壯 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道我有一天會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上就會有同理心 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們學會兒子被指控時 , 她沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年11月見面 , aicha會告訴你這怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我遭受許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲的時候第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacaria的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否被折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的苦難對其他婦女來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對於所有女性 , 所有給予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋的母親 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須是手工 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是對女人 , 而是對我們女人、對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校 , 和年輕的穆斯林女孩談話 , 讓他們不接受自己很年輕的意願結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免他們結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	主持人:我想說我從阿里卡學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員開會 , 那是個非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時在美國我們這些家庭成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都很緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼要和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼要和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們彼此想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們了解彼此的名字之前 , 或任何事之前 , 我們都擁抱了和哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個有幫助的圈子裡 , 有人在這種和解中經歷過 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始說: 「 我不知道我的兒子有沒有罪惡感或無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對你的家庭有多麼不好意思 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是什麼苦難 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該被公平地誘惑 , 被懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以這種方式向我們伸出援手 , 我想說的是 , 那是個冰箱 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都告訴我們的故事 , 我們都和人類連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午結束時 , 午餐後大約有三小時 , 我們會覺得自己永遠都知道 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅能在現在的情況下如此慷慨 , 以及當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子的做法 , 還有她自己的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過過這麼艱苦的人 , 來自完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常珍視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是為了害怕他人 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這實在太難了 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能認識誰 , 我不知道 , 還是跟我很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 阿里卡哈 , 你有幾個字來結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	伊莎貝爾:我想說我們必須試著認識其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須慷慨慷慨 , 你的心一定是慷慨的 , 你的心智必須是慷慨的 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定是包容的 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們會一起生活在和平中 , 互相尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想要說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多地方都缺乏乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師michaelpritchard做了一件事情 , 發明可攜式的救命過濾器 , 幾秒鐘 , 讓tedglobal飲用最令人驚訝的示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、展示、設計、全球議題、發明、水、水、
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelprichard的水過濾器變成了不可思議的飲用水飲用 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事情 。
the first thing is water .	首先是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都很享受在研討會上提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自像這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計數字會說你們之中有一半的人會受痢疾 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	過去我談了很多關於統計學的議題 , 以及為所有人提供安全飲用水的條件 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎不會經歷 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經搞清楚為什麼了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的思維 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法去思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就關掉:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的思維來告訴你們 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順便說一下 , 既然我在說話 , 世界上還有一萬三千人現在正在患痢疾 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛剛死去 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了救生員瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部分人一樣 , 2004年聖誕節過後的那天 , 當我在看亞洲海嘯爆發的消息時 , 在電視上演出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘 , 被迫喝污染的水 , 或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的困住了我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 颶風卡崔娜陷入美國的一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 ! 」 我心想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級體上嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相拍攝電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週和幾個月 , 在我的廚房裡 , 我太太太太對我很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過一些失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想到了 , 救生員瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談科學的一部分 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救命之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以這肯定會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救生員只有15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 什麼都沒有通過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好吧 , 我要給你們一些示範 。
would you like to see that ?	你會想看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間設定 , 所以我猜我應該這麼做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津的美好城市 。
so someone's done that up .	所以 , 有人這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城 , 所以我做的是 , 我已經從河流cherwell找到一些水 , 河流流過這裡 , 這是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想著 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區之中 , 水就不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我把一些東西加進去 。
and this is from my pond .	這是我的池塘 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞到一口氣 , 攝影師 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們要把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelprichard:好的 , 我們有一些從污水農場跑來的 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以我要把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 我們就開始了 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有一些碎片和碎片 , 把它黏在裡面 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我這裡有一份禮物 , 來自我朋友的兔子 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救命瓶真的很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水吸起來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一根青蛙來展示給你們看 。 讓我們把那根糞便放進去 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我要把這個非常骯髒的水放到這裡 , 你還想喝一杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 開始吧 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 , 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這些都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶壺打開 , 無菌飲用水就會出現 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得要快點 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	就這樣 , 請注意電力 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、無生命的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來吧 , 克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯的節目 , 其他的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好吧 , 世界上數以千計的人都被使用過 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持六千公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當疫情爆發時 , 使用失敗的技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把車子送出去 , 把一個新的車子放進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	這對另外六千公升是好的 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾週後 , 我們設立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入難民營 , 得到安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播 , 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就變成自我繁殖 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但用不同的方式思考 , 運送這些資料 , 人們可以留下來 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自己製造無菌飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上計算時 , 你就會被搞錯了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 思考不同 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不用運送水 , 用人造過程來做 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從上面撿起水 , 免費 , 運送到那裡 , 然後把它丟到山上、河流和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它變得無害 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用生命安全的瓶子 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以使用其中一個 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry的罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理二萬五千公升的水 ; 這足夠一個四個家庭 , 三年來 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天大約有半分錢來跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 在使用水的時候 , 媽媽和小孩不再需要每天四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要花了八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 目標是要減少沒有安全的飲用水的人數 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	為了將它放入情境中 , 英國政府每年花費大約一百二十億英鎊在外國援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼就這樣停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有兩百億美金 , 每個人都可以取得安全飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以 , 每年有三十五億人受苦 , 而每年死亡的兩百萬個孩童都會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•阿什德宣稱我們生活在歷史上的一刻 , 權力從來沒有改變過 。 在tedxbrusel的演講中 , 他把他所看到的三大全球轉變列出來 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化 , 世界文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	帕迪•阿什德:全球的權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在19世紀末 , 有一首非常有名的英文詩人寫的詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教堂的大腦中 , 有人說是回音 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: 「 在夏天的愛德華山丘上 , 帶著溪流的流動 , 我聽見了遠方的鼓聲 , 像夢裡的聲音、距離、距離很近、很近、很低、很大聲 , 很快就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩歌感興趣的人 , 詩是《沙波爾夫人》的一首詩 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但霍斯曼明白了 , 在尼爾森的交響曲中也聽過它 , 就是19世紀長、炎熱的夏季穩定性夏天即將接近近 , 我們即將要搬進歷史中最嚇人的一段時期 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士們 , 這些經常都伴隨著亂流 , 血流經 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們是被譴責的 , 如果你想活在歷史上的那一刻 , 當那些建立權力的秩序開始改變和新的看法 , 世界上存在的新勢力開始形成形式 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到它 , 幾乎每次都很亂 , 極度困難 , 通常都非常血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一下 , 它每一世紀就會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會說 , 上一次發生了 , 那就是霍斯曼所感受到的 , 以及古老國家的權力 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨越大西洋 , 到美國的新興權力──美國一世紀初的美國 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空中 , 過去的歐洲權力在上個世紀的兩場血腥災難中 , 第一部分和第二部分:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 這兩者是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於新的維度我想說的是從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但我們來談談談權力的轉變 , 會發生在世界上 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天發生的是 , 在某種意義上 , 恐怖 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們見過後續的權力轉變了希臘傳承到羅馬的權力 , 以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉變 , 但我們看到了有點不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只從國運到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今正在發生的是 , 執行責任的權力 , 以法律的制度 , 在國家的制度中 , 現在已經被移民到非常大的全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化的權力 , 但實際上是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國際舞台上 , 權力是指責法律規則 , 在國際舞台上 , 權力不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球階段 , 權力如下:網際網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢的力量 , 改變了這個巨大的金錢區 , 現在交易所需的金錢要有32倍 , 它應該要來財務改變 , 如果你喜歡的 , 金錢設備將我們帶到我們的膝蓋 , 現在 , 跨國企業的權力 , 經費大於中型的預算 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些人生活在一個完全沒有規範的全球空間裡 , 不受法律規範 , 人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	此時此刻 , 這會成為強大的一刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	對那些擁有最多權力的人來說 , 總是適合在空間中運作的權力 , 沒有限制 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 早或晚 , 沒有規範的空間 , 不再受法律的限制 , 不只是你想要的事物 , 國際貿易 , 網路等等 。 還有你不想要的事物 , 國際犯罪 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9/11的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 然而 , 那些居住的居民 , 那個空間可以攻擊你 , 即使是在你一個明亮的十一月早上最具代表性的城市 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有60%的400萬美金被用來資助911事件 , 實際上通過雙胞胎塔 , 9/11被摧毀 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網際網路、衛星廣播機 , 來圍繞他們的毒藥 , 這關乎摧毀我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	更早或更早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力的統治必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	假如我相信我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的力量 , 那麼我們這個時代的其中一個挑戰就是把治理帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 數十年前的我們將會成為更大或更少的混亂 , 我們能達成目標:將治理帶入全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在談政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要建立一些全球民主機構 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順便說一下 , 我自己的看法 , 女士們先生們 , 這種看法不太可能發生在聯合國機構裡 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個可以合法化國際行動的手段 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球各地的治理時 , 我的猜測不會發生在聯合國機構的創作中 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 由強大的力量組成 , 創造出以治療為基礎的系統、條約的協定 , 來管理這個全球的空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:協定的組織 , 完全以治療為基礎的組織 , 強而有力的 , 能夠保持最強大的美國 , 如果必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開端 , 創造出以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:現在我們知道 , 我們必須組合一個機構 , 它有能力將治理帶給金融空間給金融空間 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是g20所謂的 「 條約性的機構 」 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等一下再回來談談 , 那就是如果你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 制定規則 , 來填補治理空間 , 那會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	那是個大問題 , 我們只要一秒就回來了 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你經由這些亂流時間傳遞 , 那麼我們的成功取決於我們的大量測量值 , 取決於我們的能力 , 把合理的管理帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要跟這樣的觀眾談話 , 但權力不僅僅是垂直的轉變 , 也是橫向的轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會說故事 , 文明歷史 , 被文明收集到海洋 , 和地中海的第一批文明 , 近期在西方國家的權力上 , 越來越多的西方國家 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到一個基本的權力轉移 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離大西洋的國家聚集在大西洋的邊緣 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這就從經濟力量開始了 , 但這也是它始於的開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 遍及世界其他發展權力 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這不是從西方移轉到東方 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得一提的是 , 美國在地球上保有最強大的國家 , 未來十年 , 十五年 , 但她擁有的權力背景現在徹底改變了 ; 它徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從50年以來 , 最不尋常的歷史中 , 我們有一個完全不道德的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每個羅盤對或對抗的需求都必須被華盛頓一個單一大腸桿子所引發 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的例子 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的是比較正常的歷史 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多重世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	直到現在 , 美國是我們世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們仍然是最強大的國家 , 但他們將是世界越來越多的強權國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的另一種權力中心 , 當然 , 我的猜測是 , 中國對偉大的中心並不平滑 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	當中國在自由經濟後 , 她的社會就會變得很糟糕 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是一個不同的討論 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 你看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到這個世界現在看起來越來越像19世紀的歐洲人
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀 , 一個偉大的英國外交秘書 , 名稱是 「 歐洲權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五邊的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國經常扮演著平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林一起合作 , 英國和維也納和羅馬結合 , 提供一個平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由單一世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的盟友nato , 戰警 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力 , 意味著固定的聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但多重的權力意味著轉移和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	那就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們越來越會看到我們的聯盟沒有修正 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交部長曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共通的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會逐漸看到 , 即使西方國家也要伸出援手 , 超越大西洋電廠的舒適圈 , 來和他人聯盟 , 如果我們想把事情做好的話 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家不夠好 ; 我們必須讓其他人參與 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗最後一次 , 西方嘗試去做這件事 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是400年之初我說400年是因為它是奧托曼帝國的末日 , 西方制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界各個角落推行和散播 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家聚集了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行、國際貨幣基金--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我預測一下 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經到了400年 , 那時西方的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國當然 , 他們永遠不會自己涉及到世界各地和平的和平 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	對嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷特下服務 , 在藍色旗幟下 , 在聯合國的指令下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	索馬利海盜最大的海報如何處理索馬利亞海盜的問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的內臟內容 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商人主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要讓海道保持開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	越來越多的人 , 我們會和我們不共享價值的人做生意 , 而在此刻 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	它是一種全新的觀點 , 現在正在出現 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今在我們的現代世界裡 , 因為網路 , 人們一直在談的那種東西 , 一切都和一切有關聯 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被鎖起來 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 在以前從來沒有發生過這種情況下 , 從來沒有發生過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 總是存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是關於管理國家之間的關聯 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切連結在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	墨西哥的豬流感 , 查爾斯在24小時後就遇到了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟失敗了 , 整個崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的步伐中有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地相互關聯 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家單獨行動的概念 , 不和他人連結 , 不和他人合作 , 不再是一個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為國家的採取行動 , 不管是它本身 , 也不足以控制它自己的領土 , 因為在國外國家的影響已經開始影響到它們的內部 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一場年輕的軍人 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家辯護一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時候敵人就在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談我的國家防禦 , 我必須談談健康的防禦 , 因為流行病是對我的安全的威脅 , 我必須和農業部談 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我必須和產業部談談 , 因為我們的希臘基礎建設的脆弱 , 如同我們從網路戰場看到的 , 來對我們的敵人說話 , 我必須跟我國的親戚們談 , 因為在我國的房子裡 , 我們的房子是77個 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	國家的安全不再僅僅是軍人和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它是將其機構的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式 , 垂直階級制度 , 任務專門化 , 指令結構完全錯誤 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在企業裡 , 你知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 女士們先生們 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	網絡很重要的能力 , 不論在你的政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	以下是shdown的第三條法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便說一下 , 不要問我 「 阿許頓第一定律 」 的第二定律 , 因為我還沒有發明這些 ; 如果有第三定律 , 聽起來會比較好嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	艾許諾的第三個法則是 , 在現代時代 , 每件事都和一切連結在一起 , 最重要的是你能做的事 , 就是你能和其他人做些什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊紀律 , 不論你是企業的重點 , 你的內部部部門 , 和他人建立關係的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這點 , 在工業界 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一件事情 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這個例子 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在是以以前從來沒有完全相同的方式結合在一起的 , 那也是我們彼此共享的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主宰我們國家安全的概念不再足夠 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的盟友 , 像娜塔 , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	情況不再是如此 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著 , 我和敵人的命運越來越多 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官時 , 在1970年代和蘇聯的日內瓦談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方都了解到零和遊戲是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人共有命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的一個大障礙 , 是以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 他們不了解他們共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士們 , 一直以來 , 遠見者和詩人的主張變成了我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我將以一首詩作結 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 把鐘聲發送給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 因為我涉及到人類 , 不要要求鐘聲 , 它會為他發聲 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•唐恩是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找長壽和健康的路徑 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區 」 , 他們的老人和vim和vigor一起生活 , 在tedxtc記錄年齡的社區 , 他分享了9個共同飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們在過去一百歲以上流行 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、科學、科學、生命 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+1
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	所謂的丹麥雙胞胎研究證實 , 一般人的壽命只有百分之十 , 在某些生物限制下 , 是由我們的基因所決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	剩下的90%是由我們的生活方式主宰 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區域的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找到長壽的真相 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人長壽的最佳公式 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘飲食 , 或墨西哥飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	美國農業部的食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們什麼 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 有很多困惑 , 能幫助我們活得更久 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉 , 還是要吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到供應 , 你應該帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些激素還是逆轉性呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是要玩嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是與國家地理頻道合作 , 國家老化研究所 , 找出四個人口明確確確認地理定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後把一群專家帶到那裡 , 以準確的方式走過這些人的做法 , 將跨文化的分散下去 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後 , 我要告訴你們這個幻想是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先我要揭露一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你真的努力去活一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國5000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	儘管它是美國成長最快的人口 , 但卻很難達到100人 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是為了長壽而設計 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為 「 繁榮成功 」 。
i love that word .	我愛那個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁榮成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 你的孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在演化的效應完全消失之後 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是一隻老鼠 , 或一隻大象 , 或中間的人類 , 相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以要讓它變成一百歲 , 你不只需要有很好的生活方式 , 你還得要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情會讓我們變老 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 膝蓋毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以流動 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來排列 , 我們就能得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 裡面有 「 t 」 。 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞每八年就會轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉身時 , 就會有一些損害 , 而損害就會增加 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它以指數的方式建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會在錄音帶上做複本 , 讓我們的朋友複製錄音帶 , 很快就會有成功的世代 , 聽起來像是垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的老人比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有東西可以減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 對於女性來說 , 有更多的能力 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線的某處 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約12年的美好 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們都可以做到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 它們大多是免於慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為這些消失的最佳方法就是看看全世界的文化 , 實際體驗到的文化 , 人們生活的比例是100歲 , 比我們多出10倍 , 人口預期壽命是十幾年 , 中年的死亡率是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸的125英里找到了我們的第一條藍色區域 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 只有在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡有男性最長壽的區域 , 比美國這裡多出十倍的百歲人 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到一百歲 , 他們還用非凡的維納來做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 102歲的老人仍騎自行車去工作 , 秋天 , 能打敗比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史真的回到基督時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是一個被隔離的銅器時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此不公平 , 它們大多是牧羊 , 一般的、低密度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食大部分是以植物為基礎的 , 牠們能帶到田野中 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一塊未被遺漏的麥麵包 , 叫做carta音樂 , 由土草餵養的動物所製成 , 乳酪是高於omega-3脂肪酸而非omega-6脂肪酸 , 由玉米餵養的動物所產生 , 一種酒含有三倍於全世界所知的葡萄酒 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最瘋狂的元素之一就是他們如何治療老人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等在24歲左右高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 越老越平等 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 不用看運動繪製的游泳日曆 , 你看到的是月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不僅對你老年的父母來說是好的 , 讓他們接近家人 , 預期壽命的研究顯示 , 對於那些家庭的孩童來說 , 死亡率和較低的疾病比率也是好的 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊發現了第二個藍色區域 , 東京的南方八百英哩 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的零 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的雌性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	它是一個人們擁有世界上最長壽的缺陷人數的地方 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的東西 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活很久 , 通常很快就會死亡 , 通常 , 我會告訴你 , 在性愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比美國平均要長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國的百歲人數有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五分之一的蟻群和乳癌比率 , 美國最大的殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是第六 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實是 , 這個文化給了這些數字 , 很明顯地 , 他們有教我們的東西 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 滿滿的蔬菜 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃大約八倍的蕃茄 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過量 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們吃比較小的盤子 , 所以它們通常會吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其保存家庭風格 , 你可以輕鬆地吃 , 只要你說話 , 他們就在櫃台上 , 把食物帶走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有3000歲的小孩 , 我覺得這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由蘇格西斯發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	飲食就是所謂的 「 哈拉、哈蒂、哈蒂 , 飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯前就說 , 要提醒他們在胃裡80%的時候就停止飲食 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花半小時才能從肚子到腦部旅行 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停在百分之八十 , 它能協助讓你不做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有幾項社會建構 , 我們能與長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運地出生在俄羅來納瓦 , 你就生在一個系統裡 , 自動擁有一半的朋友 , 和你一生旅行的朋友 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 摩艾 」 。 如果你在摩艾州 , 你被期待要分享這個反彈 , 如果你運氣不好 , 孩子生病、父母死亡 , 你永遠都會有一個人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這張特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起了97年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這意味著退休給簡單的椅子 , 或到亞利桑那去玩高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語言中 , 甚至沒有退休的字詞 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一個字會影響你一生 , 而那個字就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大概翻譯成 「 早上起床的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的喀爾特大師而言 , 他的ikigai正帶著這場火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對於這百歲的漁夫來說 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化研究所給了我們一個問卷給這些百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是非常文化的 , 那些提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	這位102歲的女子 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲時分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一個曾曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣子 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 她說: 「 這感覺就像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理頻道上的編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們研究明尼蘇達的禱告 , 事實上 , 百歲人的比例很高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的人口 , 七天的冒險家集中在加州的洛馬林達 ,
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守派的方法 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五的星期五 , 慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	當時他們稱之為 「 24小時的聖所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循了五個小習慣 , 傳遞給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 ,
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對於一位先進的女性而言 , 他們的壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	兩者間的差異更為明顯 , 他們預期的壽命比他們的美國人多11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很驚人的研究 。 我想這很快就說明了這個藍色區域專案的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套非常小的生活習慣 , 可以追隨他們的生活習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章是29 。 上帝談到的樂高和種子 , 還有關於綠色植物 , 很可能遺漏的是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地認真看待這個保護區 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論多忙 , 工作壓力有多大 , 孩子需要被驅動 , 他們會停止每件事 , 專注在他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教中 , 天生就是走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	它的力量並不是偶爾會發生 , 它的力量是每週一次完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	不難 , 不用花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向和其他冒險家混在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一位冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到人們在游泳 , 或在開關 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們談論下一本大自然走路 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化產出了埃爾斯沃•華瑞漢 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯•華麗漢姆已經97歲了 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個百萬百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要建造一個隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那筆錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出去挖掘水泥 , 拖著水泥 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	也許 , 在第四天 , 他最後去了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不像桌上的那個人 , 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他每個月仍然做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	愛德華•道林斯 , 103歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子放上去 , 扔進長尾 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她的日子開始提升體重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進入了她的根部人 , 顏色是1994年的卡迪拉克•席維爾 , 在聖貝納多高速公路上 , 她仍然自願參與七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19個硬體探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個你見過的人 , 穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 穿越撒哈拉沙漠 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我會告訴你們 , 沒有冒險比搭乘馬基登機更加傷心 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	她會對我說: 「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地將它歸為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經完成了兩次藍色區域的探險 , 這和這些共同的判斷機制是真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我要說的是 , 這裡沒有一項運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 讓他們不斷地被激發到實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的奧納瓦婦女在地板上起伏 , 她們每天躺在地板上 , 30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教堂 , 或給朋友的房子一次步行 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 來做園藝或家庭工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們就會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里就跟跑步機一樣 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 他們很享受 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一能證明的方法是脫離認知衰退 , 而他們都傾向有花園 。
