they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式建立自己的生命 , 讓他們有正確的偏見 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要花時間改變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有祖先的植株 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或緊張時 , 會觸發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的反應 , 和阿茲海默症及心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 將發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有目的、ikigai的詞彙 , 像是奧卡納瓦人 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們活在他們的生活中 , 價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一點點 , 而不是對美國人口很辛苦 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們通常會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	並不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有辦法避免過度的小東西 , 讓它們在適當的時間從桌子上趕走 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎就是它們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老年人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於信仰的社區 , 每個月的預期壽命有四到十四年 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就好 , 不論是對的人 , 都要積極地自我包圍 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗明罕研究中得知 , 如果三個最好的朋友都過胖 , 你的體重會過重的百分之五十 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 那會隨時間帶來很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	取而代之的是 , 如果你的朋友的想法是實體的活動、弓、腳踏車、腳踏車、或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點酒 , 但他們吃得不太對 , 而且他們在信任和可信任 , 那會隨時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食沒有用 , 全世界的歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 , 通常是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽問題時 , 沒有短期的修復方式 , 或任何其他的 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想想看 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最重要的事情 , 讓你能活多年 , 生活多年 。 非常謝謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水指導電力 。 一扇窗 , 從清晰轉換到開關的不透明 ; 一個製造音樂的珠子 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔娜•莫塔說:該是和它玩的時候了 。 莫塔斯帶領我們參觀了驚人且酷的新材料 , 並建議我們找出他們最好的方法 , 就是去做實驗、修補、有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	克里娜•莫塔:玩智能材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有個朋友在葡萄牙 , 他的祖父用腳踏車建造了一輛車 , 洗衣機 , 讓他可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他無法負擔一輛車 , 但也是因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 和它們是如何被製造出來的 , 所以我們能建立並修復它們 , 或是最不知情的決定 , 來決定該買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這種做法在20世紀後半葉迷失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者社區和開放原始碼的模型 , 把知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個階段 , 帶到這些元件的基礎上 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是什麼 , 以及它們是如何製造出來的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些令人驚訝的、自閉症複合材料 , 可以改變形狀、能導電的顏料、會改變顏色、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨能讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	以我手上的這個小例子為例 , 我們用它來製造接觸感測器 , 打開這個小光 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨被藝術家用過 , 但最近的發展指出我們很快就能在雷射印表機和筆中使用 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張紙上有無色的光滑粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的加密器只會在邊緣散開光線 , 但當我打開周圍的燈光時 , 整個表面就會發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料的兩個已知應用包括內部設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱色色色色素會在特定的溫度上改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把它放在熱盤上 , 溫度比環境高 , 你可以看到發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的原理之一就是 , 在嬰兒瓶中 , 它能指出 , 如果內容夠酷 , 就能飲用 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般稱為智慧材料的一些常見的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們將會成為我們每天使用的各種物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們還可能還沒有飛行式的科幻小說給了我們一些承諾 , 但我們可以用牆來改變顏色 , 取決於溫度、鍵盤上的鍵盤 , 窗戶會在開關上變成不透明的 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是受過訓練的社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談論智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解構成我們的世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合材料的了解不夠多 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智能材料很難在很小的質量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 且很少有說到它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 他們主要存在於這種交易秘密和專利 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 凱西男孩和我成立了一個專案 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 出版資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在他們能時做出貢獻 , 並集合資源 , 例如像我們一樣的創作者的研究論文和教學 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個龐大、集體的資料庫 , 內容是關於智慧材料的資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的事物 , 以及我們不了解和使用的東西 , 最終會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、衣服、我們所居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們生活在一個由智慧材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是被粉筆給燃料 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 是發明家 , 改善了從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家明白這一點當他們發表了一篇論文 , 用簡單的方法製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他當時沒有化學經驗 , 讀到這篇論文 , 並在他的創作過程中重現這個實驗 , 只用現有的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至用了自己的旋渦混合器 , 基於另一個科學家/maker的教學 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦後來在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他曾經嘗試過的所有事情 , 讓其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	約旦的創新形式是要在大學安裝良好的實驗室創造一個實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重建這個實驗 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以找到他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想要提到她的專案計畫的目標是要強調材料的表情特質 , 同時要專注於製造者的創意和技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 它們能教我們事物如何運作 , 但它們設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 來讓我們免受設計限制 , 透過教導我們這些材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelhoho的研究漢娜創造了一系列的紙張講者從簡單的銅膠帶到導電的布料
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他的製造者漢娜出版了她的食譜讓任何人都能複製並繁殖它們
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有希望的材料科學分支之一 , 讓我們能創造更便宜、更有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝作品 , 她分享她的發現 , 為一系列新的可能性打開門 , 無論是美感還是創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 自造者有趣的事是 , 我們從熱情和好奇心創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們通常會處理不傳統的角度的問題 , 在過程中 , 發現其他的選擇 , 或更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人實驗材料 , 越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在乎的大型主體 , 沒有人夢想在家中有這麼一個人 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先例知識 , 是確保我們能在未來發聲的最佳方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 依賴我們的眼睛 , 引導我們即使我們只能看到前方幾輛車 , 但如果車子可以和彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 , 珍妮佛雷諾•療法會想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛亨利:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能會避免意外發生 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對現實:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但宗教圖像和好運的圖示出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國人16到19歲的死因 , 導致死亡的主要原因 , 其中75%與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是位年輕的司機在高速公路上 , 在我面前的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這個人在高速公路上停下 , 死了 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65 ~ 0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我打破了煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs插進來 , 車子還在開 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋部署 , 很幸運地 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車停了 , 我想我們能做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛的體驗 , 只要讓我們的車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	請各位想想看現在駕駛的體驗是什麼樣子 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	走進你的車裡 , 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感知你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你身在這個擴張的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的工作任務是將它導向一部分的公路上 , 在超人的超人速度中 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的目光 , 不是為了這個任務而設計 , 但後來人們請你做這樣的事 , 你想做些改變 , 他們要做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路邊拿走 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停下來 , 看看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查盲點 , 開車到路上 , 不去看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做選擇 , 我看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作 , 挑選我們在路上的目的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些事 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺出錯或太晚 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我看不見它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 , 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技已經存在 , 可以幫助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子彼此交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛也能看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們會看到前面車的速度 , 看到車子的速度 , 或停的速度 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 不 , 車子 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們在道路上旅行 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在被出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	對於不久的將來 , 車子會在哪裡做出合理的預測並不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使你在車裡 , 有些摩托車跑來了 ! 一小時85英哩 , 我知道你有過這樣的經驗 , 沒有 「 出門 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上待了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	十、二十、三十英哩後 , 有人看過這個人 , 一旦車子看到那個人 , 把他送上地圖 , 他就在地圖上、速度 , 估計他每小時會持續85英里 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你們會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 其他的車會在他的耳中打破一些東西 , 比如說: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 仔細看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 分享汽車間的位置資料 , 分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果車裡有gps和攝影機 , 我有個非常精確的點子 , 知道我在哪裡 , 以及我有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 以及它們在哪裡 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己在哪裡 , 對於其他車子的位置 , 有什麼想法 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你們發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當fuszy估計結合時 , 甚至在光速交通中 , 當汽車共享gps資料 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機器人的實際感應器上 , 像是在這些機器人身上:stereoraras、gps、ps , 以及立體雷射 , 這些在後備系統中都是常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也將一個距離簡短的通訊收音機連接在一起 , 機器人彼此交流 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器彼此飛來時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把更多的機器人加入混合中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多章節時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 這就是預測模式幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤預期的軌跡 , 你不會注意那些包裝那麼多 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把那個看起來有點不好意思的人列為優先順序 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要怎麼做 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪位司機必須警告出路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做些什麼才能讓大家最好的警告 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼會說: 「 你必須走出路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	這取決於兩件事:一 , 車子的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道的 , 做些事情 , 他們可能不會在緊急狀況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 做司機國家模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用了一系列的三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛向前、向下看、向下看、在電話、或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測誰、哪些車子 , 哪些車子是最好的位置 , 去計算每個人的最安全路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術今天存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面對的最大問題是我們自己的意願來分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 跟我們談談其他的車子 , 我們會在八卦的海底下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我並不知道你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌牌號碼 , 我並不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請你考慮一下 , 如果你真的不想讓青少年分心 , 知道你是煞車 , 你就要來了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由意願分享我們的資料 , 我們就能為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車走向你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	x獎得主彼得•戴曼迪亞斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金實現了他的夢想 , 通過飛往大氣層 , 並在零g中體驗無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談話、太空、科技、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的第零任期間 , 位在史蒂芬•霍金的第零位 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	在座認識我的人都知道我有多麼熱衷於打開太空門 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界重力專家零重力的經驗時 , 這真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴各位這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 由於基因組學的考古獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 第一次的團隊在10天內排序100個人類基因組 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一百個名為 「 基因體 」 的個體 , 我們被稱為 「 一百個基因組 」 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特•卡爾斯 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是進入太空 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	唯一能在地球上體驗零的方式 , 其實是有偏執的飛行 , 沒有重力 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂部 , 你的重量是25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再而三地做一次 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	美國太空總署長達八、十分鐘的無重力訓練他們的太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府機構和一家公司的飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要那樣做 , 你要殺掉那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們坐在甘迺迪太空中心 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一個記者研討會 , 我們宣佈我們的目的是要做一個零拋物傘 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的很順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼要去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	對我來說 , 他所說的非常令人感動 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命在不斷增加的風險 , 被災難摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果它不進入太空 , 人類不會有未來的未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾利益 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的車內 , 帶到零飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款 , 我們募得1萬5萬美元給兒童慈善機構的捐款 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個ted人 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩個護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監控他的血液中有2位 , 他的心跳 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們的一切都以緊急事件為例 , 上帝知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭登陸設施中取下來 , 在那裡 , 太空梭起落和降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的夥伴lichtenberg和我小心地把他暫停為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗真正的無重性 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一次拋物傘之後 , 醫生說一切都很好 , 他微笑了 , 我們說 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物傘 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的把一個蘋果漂浮到艾薩克•牛頓大學 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋的椅子上 , 和牛頓大學一樣 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四個 , 第五個和第六個 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七個和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他非常開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們正生活在珍貴的珠寶中 , 在我們的一生中 , 我們正在從這個星球上移動 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這個史詩般的探險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫大衛•波林斯基有三分鐘的驚人動畫 , 顯示細胞內的破壞性命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、技術、視覺化、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我從一個有點不同的角度來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察 , 藝術、真實和美的表達方式 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己的權利中美妙的東西 , 但他們都有很多美妙的東西 , 可以用科學和數學來檢視它們 , 幾乎就像是科學家想要約會的理想結合雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 你能崇拜它 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 , 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常是在事實之後很久 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	而你現在可以推出一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	事實和美是常常對那些不在科學領域的人來說是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來形容美的事物 , 如果你了解語言 , 和研究真相和美的人 , 往往只能接觸到它 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙的常數 , 人類理想中 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數量來演化 , 這些是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被訓練成醫學插圖師以後 , 我就試過要做的事 , 因為我是一位雕塑家和視覺導師 , 我想找出一個方法 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學的真實和美麗 , 藉由動畫 , 用圖片 , 說故事 , 讓人們不見得能被帶到的東西 , 可以被教導 , 可以被理解 , 可以被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們學到的是真相和美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式卻是相對的 , 被吸引到事實和美的地點 , 不見得總是明顯的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 煮雞 , 直到味道消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我接到一通電話 , 來自哈佛的robertlue , 在幾年前的分子和細胞生物學部 , 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫療和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的專案計畫 , 來探索分子和細胞生物學中的真與美 , 讓學生能更了解所有事實的真相 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有一個心智圖像 , 可以把它當作一個大型、大型、複雜的城市 , 由微機所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械其實是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 也就是奈米科技世界各地的嫉妒 , 都是自我導向、強大、精準、精準的設備 , 由氨基酸組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械會如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能驅動細胞複製 , 它們能驅動我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想要做的是找出如何把這個故事變成哈佛大學生物治療中心的動畫 , 它是哈佛大學的一個網站 , 它是哈佛大學的分子和細胞生物學學生 , 除了所有教學資訊以外 , 讓所有的東西都能被視覺化 , 讓這些學生都能對細胞的真相和美 , 並且能夠在腦中研究 , 這樣他們的想像力會被激發出新資訊 , 以至於他們發現生命的過程 , 以至於他們如何被發現 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是說 , 你有大噬菌體在微血管附近流動 , 它們會碰到微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁上收集資訊 , 它們會得到這個資訊 , 顯示在外面某個發炎的資訊 , 在他們看不見的地方 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但它們會得到導致它們停止的信息 , 導致它們內化 , 使它們需要製造出各種部件 , 使它們能夠改變形狀 , 試著脫離這種微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛大學的科學家和資料庫模型合作 , 找出它們的移動方式 , 找出它們的作用 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	找出如何做到這一點 , 以一種真實的方式 , 讓事情發生了 , 但不太實現 , 牢房中的擁抱者會阻止病毒發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘的讀者的消化版 , 是我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 它是一個持續進行的專案計畫 , 將會持續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們看一下這個 , 看看細胞製造這些步行的小機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kinesins , 將這些巨大的載重物運送到相對大小的螞蟻身上 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會傳遞訊息給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出果蠅所需要的零件 , 來自讀取基因的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都可能沒有這些微生物 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率非常大 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫kinesin , 他拉了一袋全新的製造蛋白質到細胞所需要的位置 , 不管是細胞膜 , 不管是組織組織 , 不管是建造東西或修補東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人都有大約十萬個這種東西在你100兆個細胞內部運行 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你根本不做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家時 , 我希望你們想想這點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到了一些關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚這一切 , 相信我 , 我們就知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們搞清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就能夠控制我們對健康的控制 , 和我們未來世代的做法 , 以及我們未來的壽命多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多的真相 , 更美麗 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但非常驚人的是這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 足以察覺細胞所需的資訊 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起合作 , 讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們一起合作 , 協助我們的身體 , 他們永遠不會看到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪布蘭頓計劃在她的車上住了一年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症和她的自由工作結束時 , 她的營地變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸的經驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會、說故事、說故事、說故事、說故事、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會、社會、社會、說故事、說故事、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪布蘭頓:那一年 , 我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是一位作家 , 記者 , 我也是個非常好奇的人 , 所以在22年 , 身為記者 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的一件事就是變成隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	同年二月 , 我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡對我來說很辛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事時 , 有很多事我想要去感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都在營運 , 我決定住在一輛車上 , 要做這件事就像一趟漫長的營地旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把我的貓、腐爛的推特和營地裝備打包成1975年的一輛車 , 開到日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於生活在一個永久的結構 , 甚至是一塊碎石 , 擁有價值的人 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到別人的負面感知有多快會影響到我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒意識到無家可歸是態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在貨車是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我常常在營地洗澡 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 憤怒和對我父親的死亡造成的憂鬱 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須有全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時的溫泉被轉變為非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	幾乎不可能在任何地方停車 , 很明顯我有一隻貓 , 一隻狗 , 這真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿越了車窗 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗去吃狗狗照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能時 , 我都會用辦公大樓的員工和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者 , 我在公共休息室裡被洗了 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間車廂的溫度幾乎低於華氏80度 , 使得睡眠難以置信 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	幾小時內 , 冰塊融化了 , 很悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起公寓 , 或買不起公寓 , 讓我有腐爛的推特和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄 , 所以我待在車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我太生病了 , 晚上在我車外的公共廁所 , 我用桶和垃圾袋當作廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣候出現時 , 溫度下降 , 冰凍時 , 它們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停了個不一樣的地方 , 這樣我會避免被警察察察察覺並被警察察察察察覺 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己無法掌控自己的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我的速度從一個有才華的作家和記者變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在一輛車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商還沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的完整性、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事 , 都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我把更深、更深層的憂鬱轉化成憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 三天沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊的人一樣 , 心碎 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝醉或不喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸 。 為什麼你真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人都不認為我是無家可歸的 , 但我確實這麼做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家可歸者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的憂鬱症 , 讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得我在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	沒多久 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯特 , 全國知名記者 , 一直在談我的國家特雷特 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的論文 , 他死前一年 , 是tim的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在演說節目電路 , 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我了解到提姆•羅斯特 , 《會見媒體》的前主持人 , 談到我的寫作 , 當時我住在一輛沃爾瑪的停車場 , 我開始笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到達了點 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新寫我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是一位作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在車裡 , 和沙發衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始再寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再是無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再是隱形的 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職、兼職工作 , 並住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續污名並犯罪生活在你的車子或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 無家可歸 , 主要還是隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇見一個人 , 加入他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神能夠克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是要成為無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢捐給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是他們住的地方 , 睡在哪裡 , 或他們的人生情境 , 隨時隨時都在 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一輛沃爾瑪的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在泰國的《保險套》中 , 泰國的《保險套》 , 米塔維拉迪亞 , 帶領我們走過國家大膽計畫 , 提高生活水準 , 第一步是:人口控制 。 這意味著很多富蘭克、很有趣且非常有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	康瓦迪亞:保險套如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 , 讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	當我40年前還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 很多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭平台開始 , 追蹤一個非常成功的孕產婦健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	基本上 , 如果沒有孩子存活下來 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	第一步:去找孩子 , 去找媽媽 , 然後跟著家人規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每家人的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要減少人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 咱們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女士說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會使用藥丸 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們只有很少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不採取任何答案 ; 我們不接受任何問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去了護士和中西人 , 她們也是女人 , 做過一個很棒的工作 , 來解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	這很棒 , 但它只佔了全國百分之二十 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為其他80%的人做的事 , 讓他們獨自說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定再多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去了你們看到的一般人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	事實上 , 在那條黃色標誌之下 , 我真希望他們不會那麼受傷 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的對象是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很熟悉 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 且他們很棒 , 他們自行練習自己的家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地提供藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	就這樣 , 我們去找那些被視為解決方案的成因 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論那裡有人 , 你都可以看到船上有女人 , 賣的是漂浮的市場 , 賣香蕉、螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強 , 泰國人民是佛教 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我是藍色的 , 而不是黃色的水 , 讓僧侶發出神聖的水 , 用藥和保險套來餵養家人 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片是全國各地送來的 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	有些村落的僧人自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女士說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何讓人類更美好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過25萬人被教導要用新的字母來規劃家庭規劃a、出生、保險套、保險套、紫外線
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	接著 , 我們有蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你扔骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落任何預期規劃 , 你就會往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如 , 「 媽媽每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 , 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 , 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 再來一次 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育、娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校裡做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有保險套的競賽 , 我們有兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久之後 , 保險套就被視為女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說鑽石不會讓保險套成為女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進了第一項微型信貸計劃 , 組織了這計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想借給實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以借出貸款給我們 。 」
and that was run by them .	他們也經營了 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年之後 , 它仍然在發生 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 , 它不是真正的銀行 , 而是一個資金額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行這個組織 , 由村民自己主導 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能根本看不到一個泰國人 , 總是女人 , 女人 , 女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著我們認為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是七月第四日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供大量昆蟲 , 尤其是 , 尤其是 , 美國男士去排隊前面 , 就在他家的大使期間 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們一個非常適當的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然快到了午餐時間 , 他們說: 「 好的 , 我們會給你午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的棉花 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你有兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物是漢堡或熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗會更符號 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	接下來是這個 , 年輕人叫威廉•龐姆 , 他為美國國際組織工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他的血液含量很大 , 因為他的熱狗被吃了一半 , 而且他很開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多新聞 , 也讓一些人憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來 , 我會幫你做很多事 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	總之 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟著我們 ? 或者我們追蹤可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的例子 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 也沒有很多醫生 。
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但每個人都可以改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病來了 , 到了泰國 , 我們得要停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否認、否認、否認 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以我們的工作沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去了軍隊 , 要求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們有比政府多了 , 他們的槍比政府多了 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能協助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數據後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 你可以使用所有的電台 , 電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們才去到空氣波 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	接著 , 很快就有了新的首相 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 米謝 , 你能來加入嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他問我 , 因為他喜歡我太太 。
so i said , " okay . "	我說: 「 好吧 。 」

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和取得信用 。

so , that was done .	所以 , 這已經完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	金錢從公司變成村落的移植 。

everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進來 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你借錢之前 , 你需要受過訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信如果你想要幫助貧窮的人 , 那些生活在貧窮的人 , 能取得信用一定是人權 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會覺得自己是個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會讓你有一陣子的微笑 。 在ted2013年 , 克萊納多•德摩摩 , 智慧型手機驅動的mini機器人 , 可以和你一起動步行 , 幻燈片會讓你有一杯咖啡橫跨桌 , 並對你做出可程式的表情做出反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個微型機器人 , 由你的手機發電 ,
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 你們當中有多少人在家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不太多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 其實 , 如果你不包含房間裡有機器人 , 你家裡有多少人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們試圖解決的romotive我和romotive20個書呆子都很著迷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八、八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是一個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小可攜帶式的機器人 , 它不只能負擔得起 , 也必須是人們真正想要帶回家 , 帶著他們的孩子 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不會很可怕或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善且可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個用你已經知道的裝置 , 愛你的iphone是他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造出一個可以wi-fi和電腦視覺的機器人 , 可以做到150美元 , 這大約是過去所需的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他正處於生物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上是在裝置上攝影機 , 跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我躲下去 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很溫暖 , 所以他會盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他就會跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來到這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。

thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是在兩個智慧裝置之間的雙向音頻和影像 。
