and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州貝蒂市時 , 我公開演講給一群中學學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果在ted這裡演講的話 , 比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 它會試著把一千二百二十二歲孩子的注意力集中在45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起就有一個問題困住了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該在哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想大家都有一種感覺:地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 下一代 , 他們必須去外太空或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是事實嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有什麼值得我們探索的嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物史上最愛的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁•貝尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他的做法是從菸草植物中感染的汁液 , 他會通過較小、較小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了那個時刻 , 他覺得一定有些東西比當時所知最小的細菌還小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字 , 名字是他的神秘經理 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為拉丁文為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在發現病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們打開了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒是由地球上大部分的基因信息組成 , 遠超過所有其他形式的生命信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關 , 比如天花的根除 , 和子宮頸癌疫苗的進展 , 我們現在知道 , 大部分是由人類乳突病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這並不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們不知道地球上大部分的遺傳信息 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做的不僅僅是滑雪表面 , 從特定物種來檢視個人基因組 , 而是去檢視全部的新紀錄 , 我們周圍的微生物群落 , 及記錄這些基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧從土壤到皮膚 , 及中間的所有東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們定期做這件事 , 來找出疾病爆發的原因 , 正是它們造成的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上拿了一支娜莎白 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們常常會去尋找呼吸道的病毒 , 像是流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到的是大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究遺傳信息 , 當然 , 我們會發現許多人的遺傳信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大多來自鼻子裡完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到一些非常令人驚訝的東西 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 在你的鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合我們以前從未見過的植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於研究這種數據的小組 , 我們當中有一些人開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的東西 。 它就像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡百分之二十的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即便在相對較嚴格的血液中 , 大約百分之一到2%的暗物質無法被分類 , 也無法和我們之前見過的任何東西配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人工藝品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度的定序工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越準確時 , 我們已經確定這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設只在它們的本質上 , 有一種非常令人興奮的可能性存在:在這個生命中 , 被埋藏在這個基因信息中 , 這些信息的特徵是尚未被發現的 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索a、t、c、g的弦時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生活方式 , 比如beijerinck , 會徹底改變我們對生物的本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許這會讓我們辨識出一種癌症的原因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情來源 , 或可能在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣佈 , 和史丹佛、加州理工學院、加州理工學院的同事們 , 我們目前正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新的生命形式 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知情病毒 , 創造地球上大部分的遺傳信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆我們可能完全不知道一種新的生活方式 , 真的就在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	事實是 , 我們可能已經查過地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能發現外頭所有的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的善良教了下一代的探險家們 , 像那位來自威斯康辛的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為 , 如果我們把這一課說成這樣:不要假設我們現在認為的是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇探索的領域裡 , 走過暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊無人知 , 他們等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後面的漢堡 , 討論一個更迫切的問題:我們物種的生存 。 他說 , 解決全球暖化的第一步是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙、宇宙、
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•迪奇在我們宇宙中的位置上 , 在我們的位置上 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走上肢體 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想要從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的歷史都已經被知道了 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其它東西 , 都很適合維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像過去的思維和現存 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現在 , 這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的概念是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可置信的 , 而內部是我們所擁有的 , 我們只需仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒辦法去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家已經知道的是 , 對大部分人類歷史所相信的 , 人類其實不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	如史蒂芬霍金所說 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面 , 繞著一個典型的恆星繞著軌道繞著一個典型的星球 , 在傳統銀河系的郊區 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	所有人都知道的兩件事的第一件事 , 就是說我們處在一個非常不尋常的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二個是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩種深層的真理視為生存的真相 , 告訴你們生命的決策 , 那它們似乎有點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不會阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 所以讓我從第二個例子開始 。 嗯 , 這個典型的地方是嗎 ? 讓我們看看四周 , 看看一個隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學庫 , 這一點也不典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要走幾百英哩 , 回到同一個方向 , 再回頭看 , 你看不到任何一面牆或化學雕像 , 你看到的都是藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系中出現 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何銀河系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們在銀河外 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的銀河 , 上面有螺旋的手臂在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然沒有一個典型的地方在宇宙中 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 你必須走一千倍的路到星際空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那這看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 非常昂貴 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境--星際空間的視野--從星際空間的角度來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能把燈關掉 , 請看 , 這樣我們能看到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你在星際空間中看到的星際空間是完全漆黑的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	如果你在看最近的星星 , 那星就被爆炸成超新星 , 你就直接盯著它盯著你看 , 當它照亮到你的時候 , 你仍然不會看到任何一隻小生物 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的大小和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管事實上超新星太亮了 , 所以很棒的一場活動 , 它會在幾光年內死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 它是如此遙遠 , 你甚至不會看到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	在絕對零度之上 , 它也非常寒冷 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它很空白 。 真空的密度比地球上最高的真空還要低一百萬倍 。 所以 , 一般的地方是來自這個地方的不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們如何知道距離如此遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 如此外星人 , 從我們習以為常的環境中呢 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球我們的環境 , 以我們的形式創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 看看比我們剛剛看到的更遠的地方--我指的是望遠鏡 , 你會看到像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 quasar 」 。 原本的 「 quasars 」 意思是 「 量子星 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	也就是說 , 看起來有點像星星 , 但不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質瓦解成了超大質量黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場引力崩潰了一些能量 。 其中一些物質 , 以極大的噴射機的形式 , 照亮了葉子 , 照亮了幾兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像這樣的噴射機物理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不能馬上存活下來 , 語言會在試圖描述其中一個噴射器會是什麼樣子的情況下 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像是體驗超新星爆炸 , 但在時間點和數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 幾十億年後 , 那個噴射機在宇宙的另一邊 , 有些化學污垢可以準確地描述、模型 , 並預測 , 最重要的是 , 你的參考性質 , 在現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個實體系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的工作模型 , 其它的 「 量子 」 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的表面圖像 , 它還包含了它的解釋性模型 , 包含了相同的數學關係 , 以及因果關係結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這才是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 相信哪一個結構相似 , 其它的結構會隨著時間而增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這種實體物體 , 和它們可能的不同 , 不論它們的數學和因果結構是一樣的 , 都會隨著時間不斷地做更多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是一個不一樣的化學寶石 。 這個化學寶石有普遍性的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構含有著不斷的精確度 , 萬物的結構 。 這個空間 , 而不是宇宙的其他地方 , 它是一個包含在整個物理現實的結構和因果的本質 。 所以 , 遠離物理的原理 , 物理定律允許這個 , 甚至強迫它發生在現實世界中最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和我們的環境 , 形成我們與宇宙的其他部分的特殊關係呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的筆記 , 我是說 , 這是真的 , 但它是錯的強調 。 真正的重點是 , 它沒有任何特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的解剖 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只需要我們在這裡所擁有的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要電腦 , 沒有任何東西可以製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體成為我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 不太有形 , 但對開放知識、解釋的創造而言 , 重要的是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好測試牛頓重力定律約三百年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但過去數十億年前地球每平方公尺的證據 , 持續數十億年之後繼續下去 。 同樣的 , 對其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 只是為了我們地球上所採取的 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星際空間中 , 這三個創造出開放知識的先決是最低的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 它是空的 , 它是冷的 , 那裡是暗的 。 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	實際上 , 這只是另一個狹義誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星際空間裡的立方體 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 這個立方體是以人類標準為空的 , 但這仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造一個自足的太空站 , 這裡有一群科學家致力於創造出一個開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 除了現有的技術 , 甚至可以從星際空間收集氫 , 形成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果有東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼能阻止我們去做 , 除了知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而非資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動提供能源 , 因為交通運輸會是核融合反應器和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再說一次 , 這對人類的感官來說很暗 。 但你要做的就是拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至現在的設計 , 看看外面 , 你就會看到相同的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看見恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些銀河中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	你可以在當地建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難做的科學可能是生物領域的旅程 , 因為它需要幾億年才能到最接近生命的行星 , 回到最近的地球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你們 , 理查 , 理查 , 但是我從來不喜歡生物領域的旅程 , 我想我們大概可以做到每幾億年一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星際空間確實包含了開放的知識 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙的任何一個地方 , 都可以成為我們一樣的中心 , 如果我們知道怎麼做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是一個獨特的敵人 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星際空間能夠創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 。 所以地球就是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制的因素 , 在這裡 , 並不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種宇宙知識的觀點或許我認為應該讓我們覺得很特別 , 但也應該讓我們覺得脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若要讓宇宙持續的挑戰中存活下來 , 我們就不會讓他們存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要超新星才能消失幾光年 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁•雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都錯了 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅性的武器去恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會在這個世紀生存 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他接下來會在研討會上討論這件事 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是對的分類 , 來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以生存下來 , 我們也無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這取決於機會 , 但不論我們是否以時間來創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是史無前例的物種會隨時滅絕
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終究會結束 。 絕大多數的物種及所有現存的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為一個例外 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用這個特徵 , 分辨我們物種的特徵 , 而我們的文明 , 也就是說 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新解釋的能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我現在把它用在目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特定的解決方案 , 只為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是對的物理學家 , 根據全球暖化 , 我只是一位女士 。 理性的事情是要認真看待科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚了 , 已經無法避免災難了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們現在最好的選項就是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 像京都議定書 , 對於經濟活動的限制 , 以及它數百億元的成本 , 或其其其它的成本 , 那就已經是個災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動甚至沒有被驅逐去解決問題 , 只是稍微延後 。 所以它已經太晚了 , 避免它 , 而且它可能已經太晚了 , 無法避免它 , 自從任何人意識到危險之前就已經太晚了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代早就已經太晚了 , 當最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將降低 , 即將降低數十億人死亡的新冰河 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這樣的教訓對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為何它沒有公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們不能永遠知道 。 當我們知道災難即將發生的災難 , 以及如何解決災難本身的成本低於災難本身的成本 , 那就不會有很多爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防的原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預先解決的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 不只是重視問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防措施等於一磅的詛咒 , 但只有當我們知道如何預防 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打 , 那麼醫學的科學就不會教你如何避免打嗝 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療 , 並專注於預防 , 那它也不會達到極少的成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此時此刻 , 世界正在發起計畫 , 讓氣體的排放量降低很多成本 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和計畫進行火災 , 來減少溫度 , 和計劃生活在更高的溫度上 , 不需要付出任何代價 , 而是更有效率、更便宜 。 有些計畫存在 , 例如在太空中的大量鏡子 , 來分解太陽光 , 並鼓勵水生態生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力解決這個問題的核心問題 , 或一般來說 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	問題是我們還沒察覺到的能力 , 不足以避免無限的幸運 , 不是只有我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板板來雕刻它們 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個是: 「 問題很完整 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一刻: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在不好的規則制度中 , 一個掙扎的國家要如何破壞貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅默揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 憲章城市 」 、 「 城市管理區 , 由國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅姆的激進想法是:城市的章節城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個令人著迷的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我認識過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫裡的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson能取得最先進的技術 , 例如手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的技術 , 來在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以防止這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進去 , 讓他們成為像尼爾森這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在規則下運作 , 說它必須以非常低的補貼價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 它的銷售價格非常低 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既不是資源 , 也不是激勵機制 , 也不是其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看過 , 有一套不同的規則是有可能的 , 讓企業賺到小利潤 , 所以他們有獎勵去簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	尼爾森的手機公司就是這類的規則 , 負責從底下運作的手機 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則的效果很好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價的規則 , 但他碰到商業和消費者想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困住了規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏的解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街燈下研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	當時真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能改變規則的方法 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則可以發展改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為有一個普遍的抽象洞見 , 我們可以實用 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人們更多的選擇 , 在許多國家 , 對於領導者 , 也有更多的選擇 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但這兩者之間的反對是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導者的選擇 , 像是給總統選項 , 提高電價 , 取代經濟體中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那就能給我們一套改變規則的規則 , 來讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能取得網際網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想看到規則的破壞效應 , 規則能讓人們在黑暗中保持傷害 , 看看美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 它就像個黑洞 , 和其鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則會讓人們處在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是要了解到北韓和南韓的規則 , 都始於一模一樣的規則 , 不論是法律和法規 , 也在更深層的層面 , 理解、規範、文化、價值、信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致他們一系列的規則非常不同 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們人類可以改變彼此互動的規則 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡 , 放大 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是暗的 , 相較於它的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 居民的數量是相同的 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家與波多黎各有一半的居民 , 和海地或多明尼的共和國相比 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為政府太強壯和壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要用良好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建造 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	中國戲劇化地展示了和規則的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的開端 , 中國是世界上高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人先驅使用像鋼鐵、列印、槍枝等技術 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那段期間 , 有效的規則鼓勵這些點子散播出去 , 能鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國脫離世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 如同世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新技術方面 , 同時也發展出新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入停滯不前 , 世界其他地方的收入都不穩定了 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國的平均收入是美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你可以看到大約百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟增長很快就跟美國一樣 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你晚上回頭看地圖 , 你就能得到一條線索 , 來了解中國規則的戲劇性改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 這裡你可以看到 , 這裡的邊緣是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都在不同的規則下運作 , 比起當時在市場經濟上被複製的規則 , 以及英國政府的管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像是縫衣服 , 製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了提高收入的進程 , 越來越多的技能 , 導致快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是典型的領導人 , 像迪士比一樣可以複製 , 當他們決定把所有的大陸移到市場模型上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但若要直覺地了解到提供他人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有在中國的人馬上移到市場模式 , 他們以某種意義上建立一些特殊區塊 , 以英國的做法:讓這個機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要參與的人都能參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以 , 他們在香港周圍設立了四個特別的經濟區:中國可以來工作的地方 , 城市很快就在那裡成長 ; 外國公司也能進來製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一個叫做深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡有台灣公司 , 讓許多人有的iphone , 他們用中國人搬到深圳的勞工做成 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	經過四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸風箏在同一個層面上開放 , 最終展示了人們可以選擇的成功 , 因爲他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證明成功導致了共識讓整個經濟模式向市場模式邁進
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在 , 中國的例子顯示了幾個點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的規模上運轉 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落的規則 , 你可以做到這一點 , 但村落太小了 , 如果有數百萬人在好的規則下工作 , 就會得到好的好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變這個國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給你機會 , 創造新的地方 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 足以得到我們能擁有的所有利益 , 當數百萬人在好的規則下一起工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提案是我們構想了一個叫做 「 特定城市 」 的概念 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個章節開始 , 把所有規則都包含在我們需要建造城市的人身上 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 來建立基礎建設電力系統、道路、港口、機場、大樓 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 誰會雇用先前移民的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家人 , 即將來居住的居民 , 永久扶養他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個特點 , 人們就會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建造 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再再而三地去做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些都是章節的捕捉 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們可以讓建造在無人居住的土地上建造城市 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	從未居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以生活在新的章節之下 , 但沒有人會被迫生活在其中 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的那種選擇 , 我們需要讓國家合作的可能性:國家合作的方式 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先是市場模式 , 然後將它擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地透過香港的行動 , 減少世界的貧窮程度 , 比上個世紀的援助計畫還要大 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這樣的合作關係再次複製 , 我們就能讓全世界的這些益處變得更大 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的授權 , 一個國家的控制權 , 一個國家的授權 , 來取代某些行政的責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這會帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是 。 但很重要的是 , 當我們開始思考這些東西時 , 會發現這種情緒 , 可以讓我們退一步 , 可以阻止我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的事 , 在我們的一些援助計劃中 , 通常是壞事 , 就是它涉及了合作和承認的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 無論是領導者 , 無論是對住在這些新的地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇就是強迫和接受的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來找一位特定的領袖 , 拉爾•卡斯特 , 他是古巴領導者 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	它一定發生在卡斯楚 , 他有機會為古巴所做的事 , 為中國做了什麼 , 但他在古巴島沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確有一點點光在南部 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一個區域 , 位於賓大的灣區 , 在那裡 , 一個條約給美國行政部門負責一塊大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯特去到加拿大的首相 , 說: 「 看吧 , 雅肯斯有一個嚴重的問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出門 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不去加拿大 , 接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新城市能在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會拿回來 。 但這會是通往現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	那麼 , 這個模型還在哪裡呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到一個特區的概念 , 讓人們可以選擇成為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是一種改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們不需要受到威脅 , 而反對的態度是強迫的 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有信任的承諾 , 投資者會建立港口、建立道路、在新城市裡 , 他們能做出更有信用的承諾 , 只要他們能和夥伴國家合作 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在一些安排中 , 有點像esrow帳戶 , 你把土地放到帳戶裡 , 加入帳戶裡 , 夥伴國家要為它負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在海岸上飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	這裡有大量的土地 , 像這個土地 , 數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這件事歸納起來 , 想想看 , 不只一個或兩個特點 , 而是數十個城市 , 能協助創造出數十億人的地方 , 也許在未來的世紀 , 會有數十億人搬到城市 , 對他們來說有足夠的土地 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在世界各地 , 如果我們在夜晚看光 , 誤導的一件事是 , 視覺上看來 , 大部分的世界已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你們為什麼會錯 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它轉變成一個正方形 , 代表地球上所有的可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經佔據了三十億人口的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到長方形的底部 , 你可以看到現有三十億城市居民佔地球上耕地的百分之三 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們會像這樣做 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從可耕地的百分之三 , 到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅降低地球上人類的足跡 , 藉由建造更多城市 , 讓人們可以移動 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是由好的規則所管理 , 它們可以是城市 , 在那裡 , 人們能安全地從犯罪、疾病、衛生所中安全、不好的城市 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	它們能得到像電一樣基本的效用 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特區城市 , 要花多少時間 , 才能建造更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	它會幫助手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以寫一些細節 , 可能進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想要讓我們跑城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放學者 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設它不只是加拿大 , 要處理雷納卡斯楚的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 也是西班牙的 。 或許古巴想要成為四向的合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約才能做到這一點 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	這樣做沒什麼先例 , 但那很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這一點 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時所擁有的土地價值有很大的收益 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付像警察、法庭 , 但學校系統和醫療保健系統 , 讓這個更吸引人的地方能居住 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 讓土地變得更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 為那些幫助建構這個區域的人的動機 , 並建立基礎規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何有低成本的建築物 , 為第一份工作的人負擔得起 , 組裝出像iphone一樣的東西 , 但讓這些建築物有效率 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節已經被解決 , 但已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有任何障礙 , 除了缺乏想像力的失敗 , 將讓我們無法實現真正的全球風力解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來作結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此順利 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享的意思是我們每人的收入都比較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:管理我們如何和彼此互動的規則 ; 例如 , 讓我們有一個計程車系統 , 支援一個研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個制度 , 我們有政府辦公室註冊的土地 , 人們可以當作牧師 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 特別是創新的規則 , 要改變規則 , 我們就不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼我們可以繼續進步 , 真正讓世界變得更美好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不用再在街燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	先鋒克萊格•凡特突破了他的史詩館探險 , 談論他的團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 以繪製海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生態圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna上的克萊格•凡特和海 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對於老化辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者大多超越悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我18分鐘內要告訴各位的是 , 我們將如何從讀取遺傳密碼轉換到開始寫程式碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在十年前 , 我們發表了一系列免費的有機體 , 大象的流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月的時間 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八個小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加入:大部份人體病原體、幾株植物、數種昆蟲和哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十年前 , 在這一階段 , 基因組學的想法是 , 到今年底 , 我們可能有三到五組基因組序列 ; 它是數百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從gordon和bettymoore基金會得到獎助 , 來定序今年的130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的副程式 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外頭有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓到這個星球上可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部份人不知道 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成了地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物只構成了所有生物量的三分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不常做的事 , 但如果你把它送到海裡 , 然後吞下一口海水 , 記住每毫升的每一毫升有大約一百萬個細菌 , 還有一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 少於5000種微生物物種被特徵化 , 所以我們決定做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了 「 火藥二 」 的探險旅程 , 和我們大海的探險一樣 , 試圖每兩百英哩採樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在百慕達測試計畫 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸工作 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨整個印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常困難的責任 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 部分協助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們用海水過濾 , 收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回岩石維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們可以每24小時定序一億個字母 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這麼做 , 我們做了一些很了不起的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 認為在我們的眼睛裡 , 只有一兩種有機體在環境中有著相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎全世界上半部的海洋生物都有相同的光受器 , 用太陽光來當作它們的能量和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 和五萬個新物種一樣多 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經把這張紙張延伸到空氣中 , 用sloan基金會的補助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了我們每天呼吸的病毒和細菌 , 特別是飛機或封閉的聽覺 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們過濾了一些簡單的外觀 ; 我們收集了數十億微生物 , 從紐約市的一棟大樓過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	我們正處於定序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在資料收集的一邊 , 我們穿過加拉帕戈斯 , 我們發現幾乎每兩百英里 , 我們看到海洋樣本中的巨大多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些是合理的 , 在不同的溫度方面 , 有些是合理的 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這張衛星照片是以溫度為基礎 , 紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本之間有很大的差異 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令我們驚訝的事是這些光受器偵測到不同的波長 , 我們可以根據胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些差異極大 , 從區域到地區 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不意外的是 , 在深海中 , 它大部分是藍色的 , 感光器通常會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當有很多葉綠素附近時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能更常發生在紅外線和紫外線上 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只要試著對我們的基因更新的評估 , 我們把所有的資料集合起來 , 包括我們的探險結果 , 遠遠超過地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放進基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但每一種我們在環境中的新樣本 , 都會在新家庭中加上線性 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於這個星球上最早期發現基本基因、元件和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹 , 我們就站在右上角 , 和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物聚集在一起 , 我們可能就有不到三萬個 , 可能有一千個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為這些基因不僅僅是演化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在一個慷慨的觀點 , 可能回到理查德金斯的思想 , 比起基因組的中心觀 , 這兩種基因組成分不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna的能力在過去十年或二十年間 , dna定序的速度已經改變了 , 且變得非常快速、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組在1995年排序第二組基因組 , 從菌類生殖器 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜鹽古菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們簡單地問這個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另外500種 , 是否有較小的基因可能組成最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做跨性別突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉基因只是小片dna隨機插入遺傳密碼 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果他們插入基因的中間 , 就會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 所有可以吸入跨性別插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中的一切 , 來定義一個必要或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用更直接的智能方法來處理13個有關生物的基因組 , 我們試著比較這些基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們收集這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173種基因共有13種生物 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	池塘擴張一點一點 , 如果我們忽略一個細胞寄生蟲 , 它會擴張更多 , 當我們觀察核心的基因 , 大約是310種 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因 , 取決於你的觀點 , 到500年最低300個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些點子的唯一方法是用這些基因建造人造染色體 , 我們必須在以口服為基礎的時尚中這麼做 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片中合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	哈姆史密斯和克萊德•哈奇森 , 我的同事開發了一種令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週的期間合成一對五千個巴巴鹼病毒 , 它的序列和它的生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個相當令人振奮的實驗當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始開啟病毒粒子的生產過程 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個聯覺病毒--小兒麻痺病毒是前一年被製造出來的 , 但它只活躍了1/3 , 花了三年 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phhix174的結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	軟體現在建立自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻開始關心生物戰事 , 最近我在參議院委員會之前得到證詞 , 美國政府設立了一個特殊委員會 , 來審視這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要記住現實是很重要的 , 和人們的想像是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何今天被基因組排序的病毒 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就對伊波拉或天花感到驚訝 , 但從這個生物體的dna並沒有傳染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造天花基因 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 正努力創造生物戰事代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的不穩定 , 未來就應該有非常少的活動來製造設計師病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞生物在兩年內就有可能 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是真核細胞 , 那些我們已經有的細胞 , 可能在十年之內 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變種子和進入這種人造染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 你要如何把他人全部放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 接著 , 我們有一個同性組合系統 , 將它們重新組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從生物體中衍生出來的 , 漸漸的葡萄球菌會吸收三百萬張放射線 , 且不會被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在這個輻射爆發之後 , 它會重新組合出它的基因組 , 大約12到24小時 , 在它的染色體分開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 或許是因為我們的旅行而存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這裡有一台玻璃珠 , 經過五十萬次輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 底部的微生物就變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張照片是實際發生的:在這張圖上顯示了一百七十萬張放射線後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體其實是分開的 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna會自動重組24小時 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的很驚人的是 , 這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們可能有上千種 , 如果不是數萬種不同的物種 , 在這個星球上 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 還有對環境和社會的議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們序列的第三個生物中 , 甲烷藻類--jannaschii它生活在沸騰的水溫中 , 它的能量來源是氫 , 而它所有的碳從環境中捕捉到的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 活在二氧化碳中 , 可以捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其使用石油作為合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將之轉換為生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來減少水分解 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有許多通路可以被改造代謝的甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威有一項主要的計畫 , 來捕捉並將天然氣場的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短暫內 , 我認為會有一種叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 的新領域 , 因為這些新的合成能力 , 這些巨大的基因陣列 , 以及同性重新組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可能有一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就像所有的生物學一樣 , 你通過篩檢檢 , 不論你是否在檢測氫化物 , 或化學生產 , 或單純的可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的作用 , 一定會很好 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從太陽光產生氫 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用會調節氧氣 , 我們認為氧化氫會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單的糖和發酵 , 以產生乙醇的細胞 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥廠生產已經在大型實驗室裡使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學物質比我們最好的化合物產出的更複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境調節的來源 , 也許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來作結 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年延遲實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理評論 , 來評估我們是否該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖把他們的文字當作律法 , 他們無法在他們禁止製造生命的過程中找到任何東西 , 所以這必須是沒關係的 。 唯一的擔憂是生物戰爭的面向 , 但卻讓我們開始做這些實驗 , 因為我們做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助了一項跨機構的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和利益是什麼 , 以及像我這樣的科學團隊所需的規則 , 我們正試著在這個領域中建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 它們是非常簡單的問題 , 我們可以設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 或許改變發展中國家能做些什麼 , 提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說快樂和成功是根根基於我們大部分人不關心的:我們往往過去、現在、未來的方式 。 他建議我們在時間上 , 建立我們的偏見 , 成為改善生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心理、科學、科學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一段健康的時間 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的概念 , 很短的時間 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	請安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大約是時間 。 終結一次 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	philipzimbardo:讓我們調整一下亞當的誘惑的對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 亞當 , 不要那麼願望 , 吃一點 。 」 「 我做過 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 , 到底怎麼了 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑 , 重點是產量、抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 衝動、反思、現在、焦點、未來焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	被保證的美德落下了對此的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩在結婚之前 , 主持性別缺乏和處女 , 直到結婚 , 感謝喬治布希的大多數 , 百分之六十的女孩 , 她們在一年內就被帶到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人沒有生育控制 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們試試四歲的小孩 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待它 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子會因為誘惑而生 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不會等 , 當然 , 其他人也不會等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 14年後 , 試圖找出那些孩子的不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 有很大的差異 , 來自抵抗和產出的孩子 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒分配的人數高達250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像一組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們不會惹上麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信和決心 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是未來的發展 , 而不是投入 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 是什麼時候的觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間的觀點是關於個人的研究 , 我們所有人 , 把你人類經驗的流向分為時間區 , 或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	你自動做 , 無意識地做這件事 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們不同於文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 牠們可以偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用一些藥物 , 用到其他的方法 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在即時情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你在感受什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們做出決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去所經歷的這種情況是什麼 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 「 過去 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是針對預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱之為 「 未來式 」 。 他們的焦點在於什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間的悖論 , 是影響你做出的每一個決定 , 完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以存在 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	過去有兩種方式 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面的、負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以用現有的東西來呈現 , 也就是你專注於生命的喜悅 , 或者說 , 不重要 , 你的生活受到了控制 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以成為未來的目標 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你是超然的未來:即是生命起源於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展靈活性 , 轉變時間的觀點 , 取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你需要學習的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 最佳的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	正面的過往 。 未來的過度高 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現有主義的現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和虛偽主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合是從過去的積極來源 , 讓你有根 。 你將你的家人、身份和你的自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的 , 是翅膀到新目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現有的享樂主義中得到的能量 , 去探索你自己、地點、人們 , 去感知 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過多時間的觀點都比正面更負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來對成功的犧牲是什麼 ?
