they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間、犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲好玩的時光 , 犧牲個人的衝動 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 。 所以這影響了他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為了工作、成就和控制而生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定和一些ted者共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 我是一位貧窮的孩子 , 在南布朗克斯ghetto長大 , 一個住在過去和現在的醫學家庭 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位有前瞻性的人 , 走過頂端 , 做這些犧牲的人 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到兩隻 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了當代主義 , 我把焦點放在過去的積極 , 所以 , 在76歲 , 我比以前更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 而且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我想說的是 , 我們正應用在很多世界問題上:改變學校的輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 改善青少年的健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療打擊創傷後壓力症候群 , 促進永續性和保育 , 減少實體復健率 , 改變了50%的輟學率 , 讓吸引自殺式的恐怖分子 , 改善了家庭衝突 , 改善了家庭衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說的是 , 許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間的觀點和其他的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果非常深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	現今有多少頭條新聞會在一百年內產生影響 ? 一百篇 ? kirkcitron的 「 長期新聞專案計畫 」 收集不但重要 , 還要花數十年的時間才會產生共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他將近期的頭條新聞報導出我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、科學、科學、科學、
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是 。
we are drowning in news .	新聞淹沒了我們 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透者每年就放出三百五十萬個新聞故事 。
that's just one source .	這只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事的確會在長期的過程中有多少影響 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個由現在長期基金會所創立的計畫 , 由tedsters所創立的 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞報導 , 新聞報導可能在50或100 , 000年後仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事都跌倒了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	拿a.p.的最好故事來說 , 去年 , 這會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年內會有影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 這有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年的主題是經濟 , 我敢打賭 , 很快地 , 這種經濟衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事會為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 咱們來談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液 , 解決問題 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	有一天 , 如果你是老鼠 , 就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近有一些故事:奈米bes , 帶著真正的甲蟲毒液 , 它們會把基因送到大腦裡 ; 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們現在正面臨60億人的麻煩 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國人不會用基因改造作物來餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經研究了十億人 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	當中國設定議程時 , 世界會變得非常不同 , 並且可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們破壞了美國身為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們把德國當作最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子身上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方法來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近的一些發現:阿根廷的蟻群現在已經散播到每一塊大陸 ; 南極洲有一個自主導的機器人 , 很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也不再需要我們 ; 一個十二萬年後的微生物 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎有沒有我們 , 生命會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但過去一年 , 我對這個早期新聞的最佳選擇是:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群更容易放到上面 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果太空總署不做 , 中國可能 , 或這間房間裡的某個人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家carolynporco展示了卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 把焦點放在最大的月球、土衛六、以及凍土衛二 , 似乎是冰的射線 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa、設計、探索、科學、太空、技術、宇宙、視覺化、視覺化、視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•普洛柯讓我們飛去土星 , 來造訪土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我會帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你和我已經經歷了好幾年了 , 它從50年前開始 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅僅是固定在月球上 , 我們還把機械太空船送到所有行星上 , 我們已經登陸到小行星上 , 那時 , 我們已經用彗星重新設計 , 在此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船 , 運送到冥王星上 , 前所知的身體是星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某事 , 去了解我們的宇宙地點 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解我們的地球 , 我們的星球 , 以及我們居住的地球 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中 , 我們可能去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 土星 。 我們曾去過土星 , 在1980年代早期 , 我們去過土星探訪 , 但我們對土星的調查已經變得更加深刻 , 因為卡西尼號太空船在2004年夏天 , 穿越星際空間 , 繞著土星運行軌道 , 在2004年夏天 , 當時人類在土星的最遠方建立了太陽 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供神秘的、科學的洞察 , 顯然 , 除了比較之外 , 對於這個系統的調查有巨大的宇宙接觸 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光靠研究圈圈 , 我們就得要了解很多星星和氣體的圓圈 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的照片是andromedanebula這是我們最接近最大旋轉的銀河系
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接著 , 這是由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝的美麗複合物 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程真的是人類旅程的一部分 , 也是一種比喻 , 來了解我們周遭的事物的互相連結 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我感到痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們 , 我們已經學過卡西尼學了 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能讓你們看我們過去兩年半拍的美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	我將專注於這次大型探索探險旅程中 , 兩件最令人興奮的故事 , 我們正在進行土星的探險 , 過去兩年半以來一直是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星與一群非常大且多樣化的衛星組合在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	他們從幾公里的尺寸縮小到像美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍過土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星和一些衛星共存 , 這裡是土星的土星 , 這裡是土星的土星 , 這裡是土星邊緣 , 向你展示它們的垂直薄度 , 它們是月球土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星的四十七顆衛星中有兩顆是站著 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼抵達那裡 , 是我們太陽系中最大的未曾被探索過的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	而這個身體有很長的好奇心 , 那些看過星球的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像是我們在地球上所擁有的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比太陽系中任何其他的身體都更像 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣主要是分子氮 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸一樣 , 除了它的大氣中有機物質 , 像是甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在泰坦的大氣層中被破壞 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成了 「 駭 」 粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種帽子無所不在 , 完全是全球性的 , 充滿了土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也就是為什麼你看不見我們眼睛的表面 , 看得見光譜的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些困境粒子 , 在我們和卡西尼來到那裡之前 , 已經有數十億年了 , 溫和地面漂移 , 將表面覆蓋在厚厚的有機水中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	如同泰坦人、油、石油等同於我們不知道的 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以在泰坦的表面溫度上成為液態 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷就是土衛六的水 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣層中是可容忍的 , 所以意識到這種情況 , 帶到整個怪異的可能性世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲層之上 , 你有數百公里的哈米 , 可以避免太陽光照射到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度低於華氏零度的350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管如此寒冷 , 土衛六表面也可能降雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六下雨的做法是:它雕刻了水族、河流和洞穴 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 大盆地和隕石坑 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把高山峰和山丘洗掉 , 沖到低地 , 停下來 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試想一下土衛六的表面看起來是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 , 土衛六的高中和地球深處一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很爛 , 很爛 , 可能是下雨 , 你可能會站在密西根湖邊 , 用油漆刷 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在土衛六和卡西尼來到那裡之前所看到的景象 , 我可以告訴你們 , 我們在土衛六發現的 , 雖然它的細節不一樣 , 但故事的確令人著迷 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人 , 它就像是叢林凡爾納的冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是土衛六 , 背景是太陽 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個月球 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是一個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器 , 可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的相機系統是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你看到的是明亮又暗的區域 , 就跟我們一樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	太神秘了:我們無法在泰坦看到什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細觀察這個區域 , 你就會開始看到一些我們不知道的東西 。 你可以看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 一個坑 , 但土衛六表面有很少的坑坑 , 意思是它是很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像是地形 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在星球上看到任何線條 , 就意味著有破裂 , 像錯 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它的構造已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 許多事件都被視為是卡西尼研究泰坦 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那時是獵人探測器的部署 , 歐洲建造的謙遜探測器已經在太陽系中運行了七年 。 我們把它部署到土衛六大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時的時間在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想強調一下這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它第一次落在外太陽系中 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	很明顯 , 在我腦海中 , 這個活動應該被標記在美國和歐洲的每一個城市裡 , 不幸的是 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是國際的使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國 , 慶祝英語、美國口音、德國口音、法語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是關於聯合國所說的 「 聯合國 」 這個詞的動人展示了什麼:一個真正的聯合國在一個好的努力中結合在一起 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 它是大規模的探索行星 , 為了了解一個地球的行星系統 , 在人類歷史上 , 一直無法達成 , 而現在人類已經碰到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我只是在談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器採用大氣層的測量 , 同時也拍攝了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我不能告訴你們 , 第一次看到泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是令人震驚的 , 因為那是我們想要的所有照片 , 從軌道拍攝到的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是一個不確定的模式 , 一個地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種傾斜的飲料模式 , 只能透過液體流來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟隨這些頻道 , 看看它們如何融合 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們在這裡融入這個管道 , 進入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片拍攝於16公里 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片拍攝於8公里 , 好嗎 ? 同樣的 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在16公里 , 8公里--大概是一架航空的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機 , 穿越美國 , 你就會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在鐵達尼亞航空的窗戶上飛過泰坦的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器終於在表面休息 , 我要給你們看的是 , 各位先生女士們 , 第一個從外太陽系表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰石 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯的 , 它落在其中一個平坦、深色的區域 , 且它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們降落的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的來源基本上就像泥土一樣 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一個沒有隔離的地面 , 被液態甲烷所困惑 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種情況 , 這種物質從我們所看到的這些管道上被清洗掉了好幾十億年 , 用來填滿低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是赤道探測器登陸的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像仍然沒有標誌 , 甚至在huygen的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	牠們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 牠變得更令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們關於土衛六赤道的電影 , 顯示這些沙丘高100公里 , 分離了幾公里 , 數英里長 , 數英里長 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百英里高達一千或一百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是泰坦的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或你不會有沙丘的地方 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再次令人驚訝的是 , 沒有液體 , 直到終於我們看到北極湖 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在土衛六南極有個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	直到半個禮拜前 , 我們飛越了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了像卡斯皮亞海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的理由 , 至少在這個季節 , 顯然在泰坦的北極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是個很了不起的神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但卻是很奇怪的 , 像地球一樣的 , 有著像地球一樣的地質多樣性 , 也是一個非常棒的地理多樣性 , 一個在太陽系中只有靠近地球 , 而豐富才是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是個小衛星 , 大小大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它旁邊的英格蘭 , 只為了大小 , 這不代表威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 它的表面很亮 , 很明顯的破碎 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現之母就在南極找到了我們現在看到的南極我們發現了破碎的系統
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是被覆蓋的 。 這些碎片是被有機物質覆蓋的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個整個區域南極地區 , 已經升高了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這有點奇怪 , 地球的南極比熱帶更熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝額外的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中 , 會引發好的噴射機 , 冰粒會延伸到數百英哩的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像編碼出來 , 把這些微弱的光線放出來 , 我們看到這些噴射機餵飽了一個質數 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 我們看到的 , 會在土衛二上方數千英里的太空中進入土衛二的空間 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我已經檢查過像這樣的圖像 , 像這張圖片 , 想出了卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是這些噴射機可能是從土衛六表面的液態水中噴出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們可能有液態水、有機物質和過多的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個適合生物的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我認為我不需要告訴你們 , 在我們的太陽系中發現生命 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 慷慨不曾發生過 , 而是在我們的太陽系中 , 兩次獨立 , 那就意味著 , 根據推論 , 它在整個宇宙中出現了驚人的數量 , 且它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是唯一我們所知道的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 我們唯一認識的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代發出警告 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你不是 , 那你會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張著名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是來自太空的影像 , 它對我們在宇宙中的地位有很大的影響 , 我們對於保護地球的責任感有很大的影響 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼拍了一張相當於前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全早期 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張非常美麗的照片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主要環狀物 , 你可以看到太陽的折射圖 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的排泄物所產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中找到我們星球的視野 , 用土星的戒指來擠壓 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件事深深地讓我們看到自己 , 並且在其他世界的天空中捕捉到我們小藍綠色的星球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	這樣的觀點和我們從中獲得的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到最好的獎賞 , 開始了半個世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被繪製 。 這個緩慢的援助 , 在災難結束後 , 隱藏了未知的土地和未知的道路 。 在這個短短的演講中 , google的拉利•卡達德達德達•德莫斯地圖 , 一個團體繪製地圖的工具 , 全世界的人都在使用地圖來繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、科技合作、合作、合作、合作、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	拉利特•卡拉特達:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 自行車納基人摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人並供應到這個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 無法幫助到周邊的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖 , 很難相信在2005年 , 只有15%的世界被地理描繪成了可辨識的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國執行聯合國的確確認了世界上大部分的民眾面孔:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但幫忙來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40個志工用了一套新軟體 , 繪製了十二萬公里的道路、三千間醫院、物流和鬆散點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? google地圖製造商 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製作者是一項技術 , 讓我們每個人能夠繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體來繪製道路、河流、學校、當地企業、影像店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名hernandodesto承認 , 對大部分發展中國家而言經濟權益的關鍵是要處理大量未受影響的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 僅僅在印度 , 數兆美元的房地產仍未被監禁 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光在去年 , 有數以千計的使用者 , 在170個國家 , 就已經繪製了數百萬個資訊 , 並創造出了一張絕對不可思議的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這也使得世界各地熱情使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們來看看目前使用者所做的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 當我們說話時 , 在170個國家 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到塞內加爾的橋樑 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	靠近家鄉 , 夏羅拉 , 班加羅爾的修道 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢識別和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市裡 , 一個使用者 , 一次編輯一個 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們尚未開發的70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落的巴勒斯坦村落登上十個月的非暴力抗議活動 , 阻止他們的橄欖烤箱建造 。 你們聽說過嗎 ? 巴西的製片人茱莉亞•巴查奇亞問了為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突的暴力 , 而非非非暴力領導人 , 有一天會帶著和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞•巴赫:請注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年間 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我和歐洲及美國的作品一起旅行時 , 總是有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 我剛從中東回來 , 我在那裡拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來保護他們的土地和水資源 , 從以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人正試著去維護一個巨大的國家非暴力運動 , 來結束這個地區的佔領 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧在地上和國外的狀況和感知之間的差異 , 正是我們尚未擁有的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要談的是注意力的力量 , 關注的力量 , 以及非暴力運動在西岸、加薩和其他地方的出現和發展 , 但今天 , 我的案例研究將成為巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信大部分缺少的非暴力行為 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採取非暴力行為 , 而是為了我們開始注意那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用這個名叫布德魯斯的村莊來說明這個話題 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要建造一個隔離障礙 , 而這個障礙的一部分會在村落上蓋 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被圍繞 , 所以他們會失去西岸其他地方的免費 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發起了一個和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你對於地面上看起來是什麼樣子的感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆壁會和以色列分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:柵欄其實已經解決了恐怖問題 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男士:今天你被邀請到一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被幾十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的激進分子:軍隊比非暴力反對更害怕 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔黨員:我們必須空想傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們完全和諧 , 我們想要把它傳播給所有巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	主持人:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔、哈馬斯和大眾前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主持人:圍籬的關節持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像上下 。 到處射擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活動家:我確信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人 , 甚至連牛都沒有 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	普特斯特:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	主持人:我們能做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴查:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很訝異國際媒體沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民經過十個月的和平抗爭 , 說服以色列政府將他們的土地的路線移到綠線 , 也就是國際認可以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抵抗力自此散播到西岸以及耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默對非暴力的可能性造成了深刻的後果 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有一項非常重要的共通點 ; 它們都是劇院尋求觀眾的一種形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一的先驅者 , 持續對巴勒斯坦議題吸引國際關注 , 對非暴力的領導者來說 , 要讓公民不服從是可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能會令房間裡的父母感到不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子更加放鬆的方法就是讓他第一次注意他放得很吻合 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	抗體會變成兒時心理學家稱之為功能性行為 , 因為孩子們已經知道他可以從中獲得父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能激勵或忽視行為 , 只要給予孩童的注意力或退縮 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇集中注意力的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終止中東衝突的核心是要把非暴力行為轉變成一個功能性行為 , 讓更多人注意到今天的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我拍攝西岸的村莊 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷的過程中 , 我看到了一部紀錄片能影響到轉變的影響 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉雅的村莊 , 位於耶路撒冷的村落 , 這個社區正面臨著非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力 , 但自從沒有人在注意力 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一場屏幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好、最專門的示範 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯記錄了一部電影 , 覺得確實有人在追蹤他們在做的事 , 人們在乎的事情 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做slidariot , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領袖們一直用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列從來沒有活躍過 , 看過電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉吉和固態運動的例子顯示 , 即使是一部小型的獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力行為轉變成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體播放者的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力演說 , 在村落裡發生 , 比如比利、尼、尼蘭、瓦拉雅 , 在耶路撒冷的社區 , 比如謝克•賈拉 , 以及史瓦拉 , 非暴力領袖會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我首先看到 , 如果我們做的話 , 它們就會倍增 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們乘坐 , 他們的影響會在以色列的巴勒斯坦衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於可以解開這種情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明非暴力在像布德魯斯這樣的地方有用 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	請注意他們 , 這樣他們就能證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•松克有一個簡單但有力的領導模式 , 全都從黃金圈開始 , 問題是:為什麼 ? 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德金、萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye、商業、企業家、領導者、銷售、販售、成功、成功、成功、販售、販賣、成功、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙松:偉大的領袖鼓舞行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所想的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者 , 更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當他人能夠做出一些似乎擊敗所有假設的事 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能、相同的機構 , 相同的顧問 , 相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁•路德•金恩領導了民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一的偉大演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠找出控制權力的、有權力的男人飛機當其他隊伍都更有資格、更好的資金
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達到人類飛行的動力 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我發現了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界的運作方式 , 甚至深深改變了我對它的運作方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	事實證明 , 世上所有偉大且鼓舞人心的領導者和組織不論是蘋果或馬丁路德金恩或萊特兄弟他們都認為 , 行為和溝通都是一樣的 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	它完全和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是編寫它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠啟發別人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我快速定義這個詞彙 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們所做的事 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是如何做到的 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值觀 , 不論你說的是你的屬性過程 , 或你的屬性流程 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 不是為了賺錢 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 結果總是是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們溝通的方式來自外界 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯的 , 我們從最清楚的事物轉變成最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但鼓舞人心的領袖和啟發人心的組織 , 不論他們的規模大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 行動和溝通來自內部 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」 「 啊 ! 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	那就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部分的行銷方式 , 大部分的銷售量都是如此 , 這就是我們多數人之間溝通的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們如何不同或如何更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:氣體的比率很大 , 上面有皮革座位 , 買車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的每件事 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式 , 就是讓我們的產品精美地設計 , 簡單地使用和友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備好跟我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼做它 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很舒服地購買蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常自在地購買蘋果的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說過的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有任何東西能從他們的競爭者中分辨它們 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 大門帶著平面的電視機出來了 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格製作平面的電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在製作平面的螢幕 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾帶著mp3播放器和pda , 他們做出很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出非常好的設計產品 , 沒有人買的 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像在德國購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你要從一家電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都會這樣做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分是:我所說的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這一切都在生物學的網點上 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看看人類大腦的交叉點 , 從上到下 , 你看到的是人類的大腦實際上被分成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完全相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 人類的大腦 , 新皮層 , 與 「 等級 」 相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責我們所有理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外界溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解很多複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部向外溝通時 , 我們直接和控制行為的部位溝通 , 接著 , 我們讓人們將它合理化為我們所說的有形事物 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決定的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給某人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節的說法 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那動詞 , 它不會 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦部位無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的就是: 「 我不知道 , 這感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你正帶著你的心 , 或是帶著你的靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我不喜歡打破它 , 這些不是身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣大腦中 , 控制決策的部分 , 而非語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做你做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼做你做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們投票給你 , 或購買你的東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 做忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給那些需要你的東西的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的東西的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 ; 而是要僱用相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用別人 , 只因為他們能做事 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 血汗和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求權力飛行的追求 , 就像那天的點com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	我們假設samuelpierpontlangley是成功的配方 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使現在 , 你問別人: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三項突變:不適合的人、不好的市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三件事 , 所以讓我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley被戰爭部門給了五萬美金 , 想出這台飛行器 。
money was no problem .	金錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦一座位子 , 在史密森尼工作 , 當時非常關聯 ; 他知道當時的所有大型思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心資金 , 能找到的市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報追蹤他到處追蹤他 , 每個人都在為langley開車 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	離俄亥俄州的幾百英哩遠 , 奧維爾和威爾布 , 他們沒有我們認為的成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用自行車購物的夢想付錢 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的隊伍中接受大學教育 , 甚至不是威爾或威爾 ; 紐約時報追蹤他們到處都是 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾堡是由一個原因所驅動 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能搞懂這台飛行器 , 它就會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要變得富有 , 而且他想要變得有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想 , 和他們一起工作、流汗、淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了支付錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出門時 , 他們就要拿五組零件 , 因為那是他們在供應供應商之前會碰到多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟飛行 , 甚至沒有人去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了它 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證據證明雷利的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟飛行的那天 , 他辭職了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 這是很棒的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你們的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有富人 , 他沒有得到有名的 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一個叫做創新的擴散法則 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	最早的2.5%人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們的早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數 , 你的老鼠和你的老鼠 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	人們購買接觸電話的唯一理由是你不能再買電動電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在各個大小的位置上 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個點子 , 你就不能直到你達成這個臨界點 , 直到你達成了15%到18%的市場入口 , 然後這個系統的尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 這大概是百分之十 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以用超過10%的客戶來試試 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 懂 」 的人 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像直覺 , 說: 「 喔 , 他們就懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到他們 , 而不是那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 這裡是這個小缺口 , 你必須關閉 , 就像傑佛里摩爾所說的 , 「 跨越混亂 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期大多數人不會嘗試 , 直到其他人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很舒服地做出這些直覺決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更自在地做出這些直覺的決策 , 被他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不僅僅是產品可用的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊長達六個小時買iphone , 當他們第一次出門時 , 你只要走進店裡 , 就可以買下一架架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面的電視上 。 即便他們剛剛出櫃 , 雖然這項技術是替代品 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便說一下 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們為自己做這件事 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做這些事 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做一些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	一個人在前六個小時買iphone的理由 , 排行六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們想要的每個人:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的成功 , 來說明創新的擴散 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說的 , 第二種成功的配方是金錢、對的人、對的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從八、九年前到現在 , tivo的時代 , 到目前為止 , 它們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下是沒有爭議的 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金非常高 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我把東西放在垃圾時間華納的dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是一個商業的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是三十到四十美元 , 然後爆炸了 , 這從來沒有在10歲以上的交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我甚至不認為它在6上面做交易 , 除了幾個小衝動 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品 , 他們告訴我們他們所擁有的東西 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個會暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過廣告 , 重播現場電視 , 記住你的觀點習慣 , 甚至不問你 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇著我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全掌控你人生的各個面向的人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀點習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做它 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心 , 聽到金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們發出沒有邀請 , 也沒有網站來檢查約會 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一受過處罰的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走來走去告訴大家他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的 , 那些相信他的理念的人 , 讓他們自己去做 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個詞傳遞給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25 , 000人在對的時間出現在對的時間 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他站出來 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	他們相信美國讓他們能在公車上旅行八小時 , 讓他們能在華盛頓的中央站立太陽 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 而不是黑人對白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世上有兩種法律:那些由高權威制定的法律 , 而這些法律是由人所制定 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到人類所制定的所有法律都和我們所制定的更高權威制定的法律一致 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好發生的就是民權運動是幫助他帶來生命的完美 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨了 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便說一下 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 的演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計劃 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物 , 用他們全心全意的12點的計劃 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的立場 , 但鼓舞我們的人 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 而不是為他們而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠啟發他們身邊的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你在哪兒停在車子裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是不是在正確的方向 ? 神經學家neilbges研究我們周遭的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	尼爾•伯吉爾:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場 , 我們要如何記得停在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是面對荷馬的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著了解他的大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從yellow的海馬體開始 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損傷 , 比如阿茲海默症 , 你就無法記起一些事 , 包括你在停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文為名的 , 它是以拉丁文為名的 , 它是相似的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其餘部分 , 它是由神經元組成 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元互相交流通過發送小脈衝或發送電訊號來互相連結
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩種細胞組成 , 非常緊密的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠在覓食或探索環境中尋找食物的個別神經元 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像我們從這隻老鼠的海馬體記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它開啟一點電力衝動時 , 就會有紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們發現 , 每當老鼠進入某個特定的環境時 , 這個神經元就會知道 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它訊號到大腦的其他部分 , 藉由發送小小的電峰 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元的發射速度展示給動物的位置 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物進入其環境的不同部位時 , 會產生不同的神經元發射 , 就像這裡的這個方塊 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起組成一張地圖 , 讓大腦不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	安置細胞也被人類記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時候需要腦部監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了一套電玩遊戲 , 他們在一個小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體內的細胞會啟動 , 活躍 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 , 每當他們開車經過一個特定的地點時 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個地方細胞怎麼知道老鼠或老鼠在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以頂部的那個 , 像是在老鼠的箱子裡的牆壁上發射一樣 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你拓展盒子時 , 激發的位置會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那個 , 每當有一面牆接近南邊 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放在盒子裡 , 細胞會在任何一個地方發射一面牆到南邊 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這個預測會感應到你周圍的距離和邊界的距離 , 延伸到建築物上 , 所以對海馬體來說 , 尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	事實上 , 在海馬體輸入的輸入值 , 細胞會發現海馬體的專案 , 它會根據特定的距離來偵測海馬體或老鼠的界線 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物靠近牆壁 , 或向東邊邊界線 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣 , 或圓形的圍牆 , 或甚至桌邊的降落 , 動物都在周圍奔跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞每當有一邊界南邊 , 不論是桌子的邊緣或牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子之間的距離 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這就是我們認為放置細胞的方法 , 決定動物的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們還可以測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 比如這個目標 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或在哪裡 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記得的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或汽車的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和尺寸 , 就像我們用安置細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的旗幟是在一個小平方的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但你讓環境更大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被延伸到完全一樣的地方了 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你還記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存你在那個位置的細胞的模式 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以找到最好的位置 , 配合你儲存的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會讓你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過運動來做什麼 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們把一些外觀的路徑放到公園裡 , 我們就知道 , 因為我們的運動 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 走回去 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	安置細胞也能將這種路徑整合從一種叫做格狀細胞的細胞輸入 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	同樣的 , 網格細胞在海馬體輸入的輸入上 , 它們有點像個地方細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠在周圍探索時 , 每個個體細胞會發射一系列不同的位置 , 這些位置會以驚人的三角形狀來呈現 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從不同顏色的電網中記錄到的電網每種顏色都有類似電網的圖案在環境中發射的圖案 , 而每個細胞的電網模式會稍微轉移到其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的這條格子上有紅色 , 綠色的這一條 , 藍色代表這條格子 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 這就像老鼠可以把一個虛擬的網格放在牠的環境中 , 有點像地圖上的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電活動會從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 持續追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的移動來知道它在環境的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有電網細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有的電網圖案都有相同的對稱軸線 , 和橘色顯示的相同方向 , 代表所有電網的活動 , 尤其是大腦中某個特定區域的網格細胞 , 應該要根據我們在這些六個方向進行的改變 , 或在中間的六個方向 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀中 , 讓他們做一些小遊戲 , 像我給你們看的一樣 , 看看這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人腦中看到了它 , 和老鼠身上看到的電網細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車位位位在距離和方向的位置 , 來延伸他住的地方的建築物和界線 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	藉由引導細胞的激發 , 來代表它 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從車子公園中走出來的路 , 這條路可以在電網細胞的發射中代表 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都可以讓地方細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他在移動的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 配對他大腦中的位置細胞的發射模式 , 用他車子停的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車是否真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能是被綁架了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去找它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找像這樣的網格發射模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置中看到它 , 在我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是會活躍起來 , 比如記住你上次去婚禮的時候 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是因為我們周遭的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就可以重現空間的場景 , 至少在我們想要想像的時刻發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞通過高密度的交互作用開始 , 然後再次啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一個我還沒提到的細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 它們會像一個指針一樣 , 根據你所面對的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要產生視覺圖像的方向 , 例如 , 當你在婚禮上時 , 會發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以這只是一個新的認知神經科學時代的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 比如你如何記住、想像 , 或甚至在數十億個獨立神經元的行動中 , 來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝各位 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全驅動力是由政府部門、私營部門、公共部門和公共事務所所驅動 。 這不僅僅是開放原始碼的粉絲所驅動的願景 , 也是納米斯•史塔維迪斯的最高指揮官 , 來自近期的軍事歷史 , 來解釋為何未來的安全應該要建造橋樑 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、戰爭、公開資源、開放資源、和平、政治、政治、社交媒體、社交媒體、社交媒體、暴力、
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆士斯•斯特里迪斯:娜塔•史蒂夫•斯特里德對全球安全的看法有多大的看法 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談談開放資源安全 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須更好地在21世紀安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先讓我回顧一下二十世紀 , 開始了解安全的運作方式 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場 , 就在比利時總部的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過300天的時間 , 有70萬人被殺 , 所以每天大約2000人 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它往第二次世界大戰中推動20世紀的安全 , 你會看到史達林立學院的戰役 , 300天 , 有200萬人被殺害 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造牆壁 。
